Acquisition (Kasb) and the True Agent of Actions
Al-Ash'ari defines acquisition and answers an objection about acquiring good and evil.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ash'ari doctrine of acquisition (kasb) and why the human does not create the reality of his actions.

Core Idea
Acquisition means action by created power; God alone creates the action's reality.

Al-Ash'ari addresses a critical objection to the doctrine of acquisition. The objector wonders whether humans truly acquire actions like disbelief and faith in their real essence. In response, Al-Ash'ari clarifies that 'acquisition' only means the action is performed by a created power, while the creation of the action's reality belongs exclusively to God. This distinction preserves God's sole creative agency while still accounting for human responsibility.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and answer
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice the objector's question and Al-Ash'ari's direct response that it is an error.
The objector's phrasing uses 'on its reality' (على حقيقته).
2
Define acquisition
Identify what Al-Ash'ari says the meaning of 'acquiring disbelief' and 'acquiring faith' actually is: acting by a created power, not creating the action's reality.
This is the core of kasb.
3
Understand the true agent
Notice that Al-Ash'ari explicitly states that the one who did the action in its reality is the Lord of the worlds. This reinforces that only God creates the substance of actions.
The true agent (فاعل حقيقي) is God.
4
Analyze the analogy with lying and movement
Examine the analogy Al-Ash'ari draws between lying and movement. Both have a 'doer in reality' (God) and a 'doer by acquisition' (human). This illustrates the same principle.
This analogy helps solidify the distinction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قال : فهل اكْتَسَبَ الإنسانُ الشيء على حقيقته كفرًا باطلا ، وإيمانا حسنًا ؟ قيل له : هذا خطأ، وإنما معنى اكتسب الكفرَ : أَنَّه كَفَرَ بِقُوَّةٍ محدثة، وكذلك قولنا : اكْتَسَبَ الإيمانَ . إنما هو آمن بقوة محدثة، من غير أن يكونَ اكتسب الشيء على حقيقته، بل الذي فعله، على حقيقته، هو ربُّ العالمين. والقولُ في الكَذِبِ ، وأنَّ له فاعلا على حقيقته، وكاذبًا به، غير مَنْ فَعَلَه على حقيقته، كالقول في فاعل الحركة على الحقيقة، والمتحرك بها ، على الحقيقة غيرُ مَنْ فَعلَها على حقيقتها، وقد بينا ذلك آنفا
For he who says: Did the human acquire the thing in its reality, disbelief as falsehood and faith as goodness? It is said to him: This is an error. Rather, the meaning of acquiring disbelief is that he disbelieved by a created power, and similarly our statement: he acquired faith. It is only that he believed by a created power, without him having acquired the thing in its reality. Rather, the one who did it in its reality is the Lord of the worlds. And the statement concerning falsehood, that it has a doer in its reality, and a liar with it, other than the one who did it in its reality, is like the statement concerning the doer of movement in reality, and the one who moves by it in reality is other than the one who did it in its reality, and we have explained that earlier.
Source pages p. 183

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of an objection about the doctrine of acquisition (kasb). The objector asks: does the human truly acquire disbelief as falsehood and faith as goodness in their real essence? Al-Ash'ari answers that this is an error. The true meaning of 'acquiring disbelief' is that the human disbelieves by a created power (i.e., the power that God creates in him), not that he creates the reality of disbelief. Similarly, 'acquiring faith' means he believes by a created power. The one who actually creates the reality of the action—whether it is disbelief or faith—is God alone, the Lord of the worlds. Al-Ash'ari then draws an analogy with lying: the liar is not the one who creates the reality of the lie; rather, God creates the lie in reality, and the human is the liar by performing it with his created power. This is parallel to movement: the true doer of the movement in reality is God, while the one who moves (i.e., the human) is distinct from that creator. Al-Ash'ari notes that this point has already been explained earlier in the text.

Key Terms
كسب (kasb)
قوة محدثة (created power)
فاعل حقيقي (true agent)
حركة (movement)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If the human 'acquires' an action, then he creates its reality.
Correction: Al-Ash'ari clarifies that acquisition only means the action is done by a created power; God is the exclusive creator of the action's substance.

Checkpoint
According to Al-Ash'ari, what does it mean for a human to 'acquire' disbelief?
A) The human creates the reality of disbelief.
B) The human disbelieves by a created power, while God creates the reality of disbelief.
C) The human and God both create the disbelief together.
D) The human acquires disbelief independently of God's power.

Key Takeaway
The human acquires actions by a created power, but God alone creates the reality of those actions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you perform a good deed, do you truly acknowledge that God is the one who created its reality, or do you secretly feel you are the ultimate source? How does this lesson challenge your daily sense of ownership over your actions?
?
Consider a sin you struggle with. According to this lesson, God creates its reality, and you acquire it by your created power. How does this affect your understanding of your own responsibility and your need for God's help?
?
The objector in the passage was concerned about the nature of acquiring good and evil. Are you comfortable with the idea that God creates the reality of both faith and disbelief? What does this do to your heart when you think about your own faith?

Rational Proof by Analogy for God's Creation of Actions
Al-Ash'ari presents a rational proof by analogy for God's creation of human actions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Al-Ash'ari uses analogical reasoning to prove that God creates human actions.

Core Idea
What proves God creates involuntary actions also proves He creates voluntary ones.

Al-Ash'ari presents a rational argument by analogy between involuntary and voluntary movements. He shows that the same evidence—temporal origination and need for place/time—applies to both. This establishes that all human actions are created by God.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the comparison between involuntary (idtirar) and acquired (iktisab) movements.
The passage uses concise logical language typical of kalam.
2
Identify the two pieces of evidence
Al-Ash'ari gives two indicators of creation: temporal origination (huduth) and need for place and time. Find where these appear.
3
Understand the logical structure
The proof works by showing that the same evidence applies to both types of movement, so the conclusion (creation) must apply to both.
This is a classic qiyas (analogy) in kalam.
4
Examine the anticipated objection
Al-Ash'ari anticipates an objection that the analogy forces the movements to be identical in all respects. Reflect on why this objection does not undermine the proof.
The author only intends createdness, not identity of voluntary/involuntary nature.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دليل عقليّ ب و دليل آخرُ من القياس على خلق أفعال الناس : أنَّ الدليل على خلق الله -تعالى- حركة الاضطرار قائم في خَلْقِ حركة الاكتساب ؛ وذلكَ أنَّ حركة الاضطرارِ، إِنْ كانَ الذي يدلُّ على أنَّ الله -تعالى- خَلَقَها : حُدُوثها فكذلك القِصَّةُ في حركة الاكتساب، وإن كان الذي يدل على خَلْقِها حاجَتَها إلى مكان وزمان، فكذلك قِصَّةُ حركة الاكتساب . فلمَّا كان كل دليل يُستدَلُّ به على أنَّ حركة الاضطرارِ مخلوقةٌ لله - تعالى - ، يَجِبُ بِهِ القضاء على أنَّ حركة الاكتساب مخلوقة لله -تعالى-، وجب خَلقُ حركة الاكتسابِ بمِثْلِ ما وجَبَ به خَلْقُ حركة الاضطرارِ . فإن قال قائل : فيجب إذا كانَتْ إحدى الحركتين ضرورة، أن تكونَ الأخرى كَذَلك، وإذا كانتْ إحداهما كسبا أن تكون الأخرى كذلك .
A rational proof and another proof by analogy (qiyas) for the creation of people's actions: that the evidence for God's creation of involuntary movement is valid for the creation of acquired movement. That is because regarding involuntary movement, if what indicates that God created it is its temporal origination (huduth), then the matter is the same for acquired movement. And if what indicates its creation is its need for a place and time, then the matter of acquired movement is the same. So since every evidence used to prove that involuntary movement is created by God necessarily leads to the judgment that acquired movement is created by God, the creation of acquired movement is obligatory by the same [evidence] by which the creation of involuntary movement is obligatory. Then if someone says: Then it must be that if one of the two movements is involuntary, the other is the same, and if one of them is acquired, the other is the same.
Source pages p. 184

Commentary
This passage is a rational proof (dali aqli) and a proof by analogy (qiyas) for the doctrine that God creates human actions. Al-Ash'ari argues by comparing two types of movements: involuntary movement (harakat al-idtirar), such as the trembling of a person with a fever, and acquired movement (harakat al-iktisab), such as voluntary motion. He states that whatever evidence (dali) proves that involuntary movement is created by God necessarily also proves that acquired movement is created by God. He lists two possible indicators: (1) temporal origination (huduth) – since both movements come into existence after not existing, they are contingent and require a creator; (2) need for place and time – both movements occur in specific places and times, indicating creation. Therefore, the same reasoning applies to both. Consequently, it is necessary to judge that acquired movement is created by God just as involuntary movement is. Al-Ash'ari then anticipates an objection: if the evidence requires that both movements share the same property (i.e., if one is involuntary the other must be, or if one is acquired the other must be), then the objector thinks the classification would collapse. However, Al-Ash'ari's point is that they share the property of being created, not that they share the properties of being involuntary or acquired. The objection is left unanswered in this extract, but the proof stands: the common attribute of createdness is established for both types of movement.

Key Terms
حركة الاضطرار (involuntary movement)
حركة الاكتساب (acquired movement)
حدوث (temporal origination)
قياس (analogy)
دليل عقلي (rational proof)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The analogy forces the two movements to be identical in all respects (e.g., both involuntary or both acquired).
Correction: Al-Ash'ari only intends that they share the attribute of being created by God, not the manner of their occurrence.

Checkpoint
What is the basis of Al-Ash'ari's analogy between involuntary movement and acquired movement?
A) Both are performed by the same human agent.
B) Both are created by God based on the same evidence of contingency.
C) Both are voluntary actions of the human.
D) Both are independent of God's will.

Key Takeaway
Al-Ash'ari's analogy establishes that the same rational evidence proves both involuntary and acquired movements are created by God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider your daily choices—like what you eat, how you speak, or which direction you walk—do you truly believe that every movement is created by Allah? How does that affect your sense of control over your own life? Will you pause before your next action to acknowledge that Allah is its Creator?
?
If both an involuntary shiver and your most deliberate decision are equally proven to be created by Allah, then what does that say about your supposed independence? Does this convict you to seek Allah's help even in your most 'personal' choices? How will you change your reliance on Him starting today?
?
The objector in the passage assumed that if the same evidence applies, the two movements must be identical. Are you ever like that objector, expecting that God's involvement in your life must look the same in every situation? Where are you resisting the idea that Allah works differently in different aspects of your life? Will you submit to His wisdom even when you don't understand?

Refutation of the Claim that Voluntary Motion is Not Created by Allah
Refutation of an objection that voluntary motion is not created by Allah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Ashʿarī refutes the objection that voluntary motion is not created by Allah, by demonstrating that the criterion of being within human power does not negate divine creation.

Core Idea
What is within your power is still created by Allah — power does not exclude creation.

In this passage, al-Ashʿarī addresses a key objection from those who claim that voluntary actions are not created by Allah because they are within human capability. The objector argues that only involuntary motions, which are impossible to do, must be created by Allah. Al-Ashʿarī responds by pointing out the logical flaw in this reasoning, showing that if capability implied self-creation, then even involuntary motions could be attributed to creatures. This lesson unpacks the objection and its refutation, clarifying the Islamic position on divine creation of all actions.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Understand the objector's claim: voluntary motion is not created by Allah because it is within human capability, unlike involuntary motion which is impossible and thus must be created.
The objector uses a contrast between voluntary and involuntary motion.
2
Follow the refutation logic
Notice how al-Ashʿarī turns the objection on its head: if being within someone's power meant it is not created, then involuntary motions could also be performed by angels empowered by Allah, destroying the evidence.
The refutation shows the objection leads to absurdity.
3
Grasp the conclusion
Both voluntary and involuntary motions are created by Allah. Power in a creature does not remove the need for divine creation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قال قائل : ما أنكرتُمْ أن يكون الذي الحركتين مخلوقة لله -تعالى- هو أن حركة الاضطرار وقعتْ مُعْجَزًا عنها ، فإذا وقعت الأخرى مقدورًا عليها خرجت من أن تكون مخلوقة؟ قيل له : لو كان ما وَقَعَ مقدورًا لغير الله -تعالى- خرج من أن يكون مخلوقا، لم يُؤْمَنْ أن تكون حركات المرتعش من الفالح والمرتعِدِ من الحمّى ، قد أَقْدَرَ الله تعالى - عَلَيْها بعض ملائكِتِه ، يفعلُها في المتحرّك باضطرار ؛ إذْ كانَ لا يَستحيلُ - عِندَ مُخالفينا - أن يَقْدِرَ القادِرُ من المخلوقِينَ علَى أَن يَفْعَلَ فِي غَيْرِهِ، فَتَبطل دَلَالَتُها على أنَّ الله -تعالى- فَعَلَها، على ما هي عليه .
If a questioner says: What prevents you from [admitting] that the one of the two motions which is created by Allah, the Exalted, is that involuntary motion occurred impossible to be done, so when the other motion occurred within capability, it exits from being created? It is said to him: If what occurred within capability for other than Allah, the Exalted, exits from being created, it would not be safe that the motions of the trembling [person] from palsy and the shivering from fever might have been empowered by Allah, the Exalted, upon them some of His angels, doing them in the moving one involuntarily, since it is not impossible – according to our opponents – that a capable one among creatures can act in another [thing], so their evidence that Allah, the Exalted, did them would be invalid, according to what they are upon.
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer regarding the createdness of voluntary actions. The objector argues that while involuntary motion (al-ḍarūrī) is beyond human power and thus must be created by Allah, voluntary motion (al-iktisābī) is within human power and therefore not created by Allah. The answer refutes this by pointing out that if being within someone's power meant it was not created by Allah, then one could not be sure that even involuntary motions, like trembling from palsy, are not performed by angels whom Allah has empowered. Since it is possible (according to opponents) for a creature to act in another, the evidence that involuntary motions are created by Allah would also be undermined. Thus, the distinction based on power does not prove the non-creation of voluntary motions; rather, both types of motion must be created by Allah.

Key Terms
حركة الاضطرار
مقدورًا عليها
معجزًا عنها
مخلوقة
قادر من المخلوقين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that if an action is within human power, it cannot be created by Allah.
Correction: Al-Ashʿarī shows that being within someone's power does not negate divine creation; rather, Allah creates the action and grants the power.

Checkpoint
What is the crux of the objector's claim that voluntary motion is not created by Allah?
A) Voluntary motion is impossible, so it cannot be created.
B) Involuntary motion is created because it is beyond human power, while voluntary motion is within human power and thus not created.
C) Angels create all human motions.
D) Voluntary motion is accidental and not real.

Key Takeaway
The fact that an action is within human power does not mean it is not created by Allah; both voluntary and involuntary actions are created by Him.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you perform a voluntary action—like raising your hand or choosing to obey Allah—do you truly feel that Allah is the creator of that action, or do you sense a sense of independence? How does this passage unsettle that feeling of self-sufficiency?
?
If you believed that your ability to choose or act exempts your actions from Allah's creation, what would that imply about your reliance on Him? Read the source again: what would be 'not safe' about that belief, and how does it shake your certainty that all things are from Allah?
?
The objector thought that involuntary motions proved Allah's creation, but voluntary ones did not. Have you ever subconsciously made a similar divide—seeing some events as 'from Allah' (trials, death) and others as 'from yourself' (success, choices)? How does al-Ash'ari's response force you to reconsider that division?

Ability and Inability as Equal Proofs of Creation
Al-Ash'ari's second argument: inability and ability both indicate divine creation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Ash'ari argues that both ability and inability equally point to Allah's creation of all human actions, including voluntary ones acquired by humans.

Core Idea
Ability and inability both equally prove that Allah is the Creator of every action.

Imam al-Ash'ari presents a second argument reinforcing that all human actions are created by Allah. He shows that whether we are able or unable to do something, the existence of that ability or inability is itself a sign that Allah is the ultimate Creator. This argument strengthens the Ash'ari position on divine omnipotence and human acquisition (kasb).

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation once. Note the logical structure: comparison, analogy, and conclusion.
The argument builds step by step.
2
Identify the key comparison
Al-Ash'ari compares inability and ability. He argues that inability is not a stronger indicator of creation than ability.
3
Understand the analogy
He uses an analogy: just as Allah creates knowledge and hearing in us and He is more knowing and hearing, so too with ability – Allah creates ability and is more able over the action.
This establishes that ability and inability are equal in the sight of Allah's power.
4
Apply the reasoning to voluntary actions
The argument then applies specifically to voluntary motions (حركة الاكتساب). If Allah empowers us, He must be the Creator of that motion as our acquisition.
Otherwise, we would have to create it ourselves, which is impossible.
5
Reflect on the implication
Consider how this argument refutes the view that human ability excludes divine creation. It underscores that all actions are created by Allah.
This is a key point in the Ash'ari doctrine of kasb.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأيضًا فليسَ العجز بأن يدلَّ على أن الله - تعالى - خَلَقَ المَعْجُوزَ ، بأَوْلَى مِنْ أَنْ تكونَ القدرة، التي جَعَلَها اللَّهُ -تعالى- دَلالة على أنَّ اللَّهَ خَلَقَ المَقْدورَ عليه ؛ لأنَّ ما خَلَقَ اللَّهُ -تعالى- القدرَةَ فينا عليه، فهو عليه أَقْدَرُ. كما أن [ما] خَلَقَ فينا العلم به فهو به أَعْلَمُ، وما خَلَقَ فينا السمعَ لَهُ فهو له أَسْمَعُ . فإذا استوى ذلك في قدرة الله تعالى-، وجب إذا أَقْدَرَنا الله . تعالى- على حركة الاكتساب أن يكون هو الخالق لها فينا كسبا لَنا ؛ لأنَّ ما قَدَرَ عليه أن يفعله فينا ، ولم يفعله فينا كسبا ، فقد ترَكَ أن يفعله فينا كسبا . وإذا ترك أن يفعله كسباً لنا، استحال أن نكون له فدل ما قلنا على أنَّا لا نكتسبه إلا وقد خلقه الله -تعالى- لنا كسباً .
And also: Inability is not more appropriate to indicate that Allah, the Exalted, created the impossible, than that ability – which Allah, the Exalted, made an indication that Allah created the possible – [indicates]; because what Allah, the Exalted, created ability in us for it, He is more able over it. Just as what He created knowledge of it in us, He is more knowledgeable of it; and what He created hearing of it in us, He is more hearing of it. So when that is equal in the power of Allah, the Exalted, then if Allah, the Exalted, empowers us over the voluntary motion, it is necessary that He is the Creator of it in us as an acquisition for us; because what He has power to do in us but does not do it in us as an acquisition, then He has left doing it in us as an acquisition. And if He leaves doing it as an acquisition for us, it is impossible for us to be [acquiring] it. So what we have said indicates that we do not acquire it except after Allah, the Exalted, has created it for us as an acquisition.
Source pages p. 188

Commentary
This passage is an additional argument (وأيضًا) that complements the previous refutation. It argues that inability (al-ʿajz) to do something is not a stronger proof that Allah created that thing than ability (al-qudra) is that Allah created the thing one is able to do. This is because when Allah creates ability in us for something, He is more able (aqdar) over it; just as when He creates knowledge of something in us, He is more knowing (aʿlam), and when He creates hearing of something in us, He is more hearing (asmaʿ). So the two cases are equal in terms of Allah's power. Therefore, if Allah empowers us over voluntary motion (ḥarakat al-iktisāb), it is necessary that He is the Creator of that motion in us as our acquisition (kasban). For if He had the power to do it in us but did not do it as our acquisition, He would have left it undone. And if He left it undone, it would be impossible for us to acquire it. Hence, we cannot acquire a motion unless Allah has created it in us as an acquisition. This reinforces the doctrine that all human actions, whether within our power or not, are created by Allah.

Key Terms
العجز
القدرة
المعجز
المقدور عليه
كسب
خلق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Human ability to perform an action means that action is not created by Allah.
Correction: Al-Ash'ari argues that ability itself is created by Allah and is an indication that Allah is the Creator of the action, just as inability is. Both are equal proofs.

Checkpoint
What does al-Ashʿarī argue about the relationship between ability and creation in this passage?
A) Ability disproves creation.
B) Inability is a better proof of creation than ability.
C) Both ability and inability equally indicate that Allah is the Creator of the action.
D) Ability is not created by Allah.

Key Takeaway
Both ability and inability equally serve as evidence that Allah is the Creator of all actions, including those we voluntarily perform.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you succeed at something through your own ability, do you truly feel that Allah is 'more able' over that action than you are? How does that change the way you view your own achievements and the praise you seek? Commit to mentally attribute every success to Allah's creation of ability in you.
?
When you are unable to do something, does it drive you to recognize Allah as the sole Creator of both your inability and the action itself? Or do you feel frustrated as if you were independent in your inability? This week, when you face failure, pause and say: 'My inability is also a sign that only Allah creates actions.'
?
If every voluntary motion of yours—even writing this answer—is created by Allah as your acquisition, then where is the room for pride? What does it mean for your sense of self-ownership? Make a conscious effort today to mentally dedicate each small act to Allah as the true Creator.

Speech as an Essential Attribute: Refuting Objections
Ash'ari extends the refutation to speech and falsehood, proving divine speech is essential.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Ash'ari argues that God's speech cannot be created or attributed to another, and how this proves divine speech is an essential attribute.

Core Idea
God's speech is an essential attribute, not a created act.

Ash'ari continues his refutation of objections against divine speech. He uses a conditional analogy and appeals to an earlier proof that God's speech is from His essence. This passage shows how the same logic used for injustice fails for speech, and why created speech cannot be attributed to Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Ash'ari uses a very compressed style here.
2
Identify the conditional argument
Ash'ari presents a conditional: if a non-liar were forced to be called a liar for creating falsehood, then similar problems arise for volition and movement. Find this reasoning and understand its logical structure.
This is a reductio ad absurdum argument.
3
Understand the analogy with volition and movement
Ash'ari extends the logic: just as a non-willing person is not called willing for creating volition, a non-liar is not called liar for creating falsehood. See how this undermines the objection.
4
Examine the appeal to earlier proof
Ash'ari references an earlier demonstration that God's speech is an essential attribute. Understand why this makes it impossible for Him to be speaking by the speech of another.
Essential attributes cannot be acquired from outside.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
The final point: just as knowledge if essential cannot be created, so speech as essential cannot be created. God's speech is not like created speech.
This reinforces divine transcendence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَعُرُوضُ هَذَا أَنْ يَخْلُقَ قَوْلًا لِغَيْرِهِ لَا لَهُ، وَلَا يَكُونُ بِهِ قَائِلًا. وَأَيْضًا: فَلَوْ وَجَبَ أَنْ يَقُولَ الْكَذِبَ مَنْ لَيْسَ بِكَاذِبٍ كَمَا فَعَلَ الْجَوْرَ مَنْ لَيْسَ بِجَائِرٍ، لَوَجَبَ أَنْ يَقُولَ الْكَذِبَ مَنْ لَيْسَ بِكَاذِبٍ كَمَا فَعَلَ الْإِرَادَةَ مَنْ لَيْسَ بِمُرِيدٍ لَهَا وَالْحَرَكَةَ مَنْ لَيْسَ بِمُتَحَرِّكٍ بِهَا، فَإِنْ لَمْ يَجِبْ هَذَا لَمْ يَجِبْ مَا قَالُوهُ. وَأَيْضًا: فَقَدْ دَلَّلْنَا عَلَى أَنَّ كَلَامَ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى مِنْ صِفَاتِ ذَاتِهِ، فِي صَدْرِ كِتَابِنَا هَذَا، فَاسْتَحَالَ لِذَلِكَ أَنْ يَكُونَ بِقَوْلِ غَيْرِهِ قَائِلًا، كَمَا إِذَا كَانَ الْعِلْمُ مِنْ صِفَاتِ نَفْسِهِ، اسْتَحَالَ أَنْ يَكُونَ عِلْمُ غَيْرِهِ عِلْمًا لَهُ، وَأَنْ يَكُونَ رَبُّ الْعَالَمِينَ عَالِمًا بِعِلْمٍ مُحْدَثٍ.
The same applies to this: that He creates speech for another not for Himself, and He is not speaking by it. And also: if it were necessary that a non-liar speaks falsehood just as a non-unjust person commits injustice, then it would be necessary that a non-liar speaks falsehood just as a non-willing person performs volition and a non-moving person performs movement. If this is not necessary, what they said is not necessary. And also: we have already demonstrated that the speech of God is from the attributes of His essence, in the beginning of this book. Therefore it is impossible for Him to be speaking by the speech of another, just as if knowledge were from the attributes of His essence, it would be impossible for the knowledge of another to be knowledge for Him, and for the Lord of the worlds to be knowledgeable by an originated knowledge.
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This passage continues the refutation of the objections by addressing the analogy of speech and falsehood. The author first states that the same reasoning applies to speech: if God creates speech for another, He is not called speaking. Then he presents a conditional argument: if a non-liar were forced to be called a liar for creating falsehood for another (just as a non-unjust person would be called unjust for creating injustice), then a similar problem would arise for volition and movement – a non-willing person would be called willing if he creates volition, etc. Since this is not accepted, the original objection fails. Finally, the author invokes an earlier proof from the beginning of the book that God's speech (kalam) is an attribute of His essence (sifāt dhātihi). Because it is essential, it cannot be a created thing. Therefore, it is impossible for God to be speaking by the speech of another, just as if knowledge were an essential attribute, it would be impossible for Him to be knowledgeable by someone else's knowledge or by an originated (created) knowledge. This last point reinforces the transcendence of God and the distinction between Creator and creatures.

Key Terms
قول
كذب
كلام الله
صفات الذات
علم محدث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that if God creates speech in a person, He could be considered speaking that speech.
Correction: Created speech is not attributable to God because His speech is an essential attribute, not a created act.

Checkpoint
What is the final argument al-Ash'ari uses to prove that God cannot be speaking by the speech of another?
A) God's speech is created.
B) God's speech is an attribute of His essence, not created.
C) God does not speak.
D) Speech belongs only to humans.

Key Takeaway
God's speech is an essential attribute, so it cannot be created speech from another.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The passage refutes the idea that God could be attributed with created speech. Are there any attributes of God—like His mercy, His power, or His knowledge—that you unconsciously reduce to created, human-like qualities? How does that misunderstanding affect the way you seek His mercy, rely on His power, or trust His knowledge?
?
If God's speech were not essential but created, then He would not truly be speaking. Have you ever treated a command or promise of God as less than absolutely binding because you doubted its eternal origin? Will you commit today to honoring every word of the Quran as coming directly from His eternal essence?

Divine Speech is Uncreated
Al-Ash'ari argues divine speech cannot be created in another.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why al-Ash'ari argues that divine speech cannot be a created entity, but is an eternal attribute of God's essence.

Core Idea
Speech, like knowledge, must belong to the speaker's essence, not be created in another.

This lesson presents al-Ash'ari's concise rebuttal of the Mu'tazilite doctrine that God creates speech in another object and thereby becomes a speaker. Using analogy and his earlier proof that speech is an essential attribute, he demonstrates the impossibility of such a view. Let's follow his argument step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Try to grasp the flow: an initial claim, an analogy, and a reference to earlier proof.
Notice that the passage is dense and uses conditional reasoning (لو... لوجب...).
2
Identify the three parts of the argument
The passage has three distinct moves: (1) the problematic claim that God creates speech for another, (2) a reductio ad absurdum using analogy with will and motion, (3) the positive proof from essential attributes.
3
Understand the analogy
Al-Ash'ari draws an analogy: if a non-liar could speak falsehood (by having falsehood created in him), then absurd consequences follow (non-willer willing, non-mover moving). Since those are impossible, the original claim fails.
This is a logical argument by showing the implications are absurd.
4
Connect to the essential attribute proof
Al-Ash'ari refers to his earlier demonstration that God's speech is from His essence (eternal). Therefore, it cannot be a created speech in another, just as God's knowledge cannot be a created knowledge.
This seals the argument: speech is an essential attribute, not an accidental one.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أَفْعَالُ العِبادِ مِن خَلْقِ الله فأما هذا أن يخلق قولا لغيره لا له، ولا يكون به قائلا. وأيضًا: فلو وجب أن يقول الكذب من ليس بكاذب كما فعل الجور من ليس بجائرٍ، لوجَبَ أنْ يقول الكذبَ مَنْ ليس بكاذِب كما فعل الإرادة من ليس بمريد لها والحركة من ليس بمتحرك بها، فإن لَمْ يَجِبْ هذا لم يجب ما قالُوه. وأيضًا: فقد دلَّلنا على أنَّ كلام الله - تعالى - من صفاتِ ذاتِه، في صدر كتابنا هذا، فاستحال لذلكَ أنْ يكونَ بِقَوْلِ غيرِه قائلا، كمَا إِذَا كان العِلمُ مِنْ صفاتِ نَفْسِه، استحال أن يكونَ عِلْمُ غيرِه عِلمًا له، وأن يكونَ رَبُّ العالمينَ عالما بعِلْمٍ مُحدّث .
The actions of servants are from the creation of Allah. So the occurrence of this is that He creates speech for another, not for Himself, and that other is not a speaker by it. And also: if it were necessary that the one who is not a liar should speak falsehood, just as the one who is not unjust does injustice, then it would be necessary that the one who is not a liar should speak falsehood, just as will is done by one who does not will it, and motion is done by one who does not move by it. And if this is not necessary, then what they said is not necessary. And also: we have proven that the speech of Allah the Exalted is among the attributes of His essence, at the beginning of this book of ours, so it is impossible therefore that He should be a speaker by the speech of another, just as when knowledge is among the attributes of His essence, it is impossible that the knowledge of another should be knowledge for Him, and that the Lord of the worlds should be knowing by a created knowledge.
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This passage is an argument against the Mu'tazilite view that God creates speech in another (like the created Qur'an) and thus becomes a speaker by that created speech. The author, al-Ash'ari, first states the problematic case: God creates speech for another, not for Himself, and that other is not a speaker by that speech. Then he gives an analogy: if it were necessary that a non-liar should speak falsehood just as a non-unjust person does injustice, then it would be necessary that a non-liar speak falsehood, just as will is performed by one who does not will it, and motion by one who does not move by it. But these are absurd consequences, so the original claim is false. Then he references his earlier proof that God's speech is from His essence (eternal), so it is impossible that He becomes a speaker by another's speech, just as His knowledge being essential prevents Him from being knowing by a created knowledge.

Key Terms
خلق
قول
كلام الله
صفات الذات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God can become a speaker by creating speech in a separate object (e.g., a tree or the Preserved Tablet).
Correction: Speech, like knowledge, is an essential attribute of God; it cannot be created in another and then attributed to Him. God's speech is eternal and from His essence.

Checkpoint
According to al-Ash'ari's argument, why can God not be a speaker by a speech created in another?
A) Because speech is an action, not an attribute.
B) Because divine speech is from His essence, just as divine knowledge is essential.
C) Because God does not create speech at all.
D) Because speech can only be spoken by a human.

Key Takeaway
Divine speech is an eternal attribute of God's essence, not a created entity in another, just as divine knowledge is essential and uncreated.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

What would change in your relationship with the Qur'an if you genuinely internalized that it is not a created text but an attribute of the Creator Himself? Will you commit today to approaching every verse as a direct expression of His eternal attributes?

Can you treat His words as optional or negotiable when they are as fundamental to Him as His own knowledge? Will you submit fully to the Qur'an's commands, acknowledging that they originate from an eternal, uncreated attribute of Allah?

Clarifying the Meaning of 'He Made Excellent Everything He Created'
Ash'ari clarifies the meaning of Quran 32:7 by distinguishing between the quality of the act and the quality of the product.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the linguistic interpretation of Quran 32:7 as explained by Ash'ari, and why it does not imply that every created thing is good in a moral sense.

Core Idea
The verse affirms Allah's perfect creative skill, not the moral quality of creation.

This lesson addresses a common misunderstanding about Quran 32:7. Someone might think 'made excellent everything He created' means everything Allah creates is good, but Ash'ari shows that the verse speaks about Allah's knowledge and ability to create well. We'll see his response to an imagined objector and the analogy he uses.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and response
Read the Arabic passage and translation to see the structure: an objector raises a question, and Ash'ari answers.
Notice the pattern of 'objection-and-answer' common in kalam texts.
2
Understand the analogy
Ash'ari uses the example of a craftsman. Explain how the analogy clarifies that 'ahsana' refers to the act of creating, not the created object.
This is key to understanding the verse.
3
Reflect on the implication
Consider why this interpretation matters for the broader discussion of good and evil in creation. It guards against a deterministic reading.
This connects to divine justice and omnipotence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قال قائل : فما معنى قولِ اللَّهِ -تعالى-: ﴿أَحْسَنَ كُلَّ شَيْءٍ خَلَقَة [السجدة : ٧]؟ قيل له : معنى ذلك أنه يُحسِنُ أن يخلُقَ ، كما يقال : فلان يُحسِنُ الصِّيَاغَةَ ، أي يَعْلَمُ كَيْفَ يصوعُ . فأخبر الله -تعالى- أنه يعلم كيف يخلق الإنسان
If a speaker says: What is the meaning of the statement of Allah, the Exalted: 'He made excellent everything He created' (as-Sajda 7)? It is said to him: The meaning of that is that He is able to create well, just as it is said: So-and-so is good at craftsmanship, meaning he knows how to craft. So Allah, the Exalted, informed that He knows how to create man.
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage is another objection-and-answer. The objector asks about Quran 32:7, which says that Allah 'ahsana kulla shay'in khalaqahu' (made excellent everything He created). The objector may argue that this means everything Allah creates is good, therefore He cannot create evil or karma/us (hardship). The author (Ash'ari) responds by explaining the linguistic meaning: 'ahsana' here does not mean that the thing itself is good, but that the action of creating is done well, i.e., Allah knows how to create. He gives an analogy: saying 'so-and-so is good at craftsmanship' means he knows how to craft, not that every crafted item is necessarily beautiful or good. Similarly, the verse informs that Allah knows how to create, especially man. This interpretation removes the implication that everything created is morally good; rather, it asserts Allah's perfect creative ability. The passage guards against a deterministic reading that would deny the reality of evil in the world.

Key Terms
أحسن (ahsana)
خلقة (khalaqah)
صياغة (siyaghah)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse means every created thing is good.
Correction: The verse means Allah creates with perfect knowledge and skill, not that every created thing is morally good.

Checkpoint
How does Ash'ari interpret 'ahsana kulla shay'in khalaqahu' from Quran 32:7?
A) It means every individual created thing is good
B) It means Allah creates with excellent knowledge and skill
C) It means only good things are created by Allah
D) It refers to the perfection of the heavens only

Key Takeaway
The verse 'ahsana kulla shay'in khalaqahu' affirms Allah's perfect creative ability, not the inherent goodness of everything created.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face something in life that feels evil or unjust, do you quickly doubt Allah's perfect creation? How can this lesson's distinction between Allah's creative knowledge and the moral quality of created things help you trust Him more deeply in those moments? Will you commit to reminding yourself that Allah knows exactly what He is doing, even when you don't understand?
?
This passage teaches that 'ahsana' refers to Allah's skill, not the inherent goodness of everything. Are there areas in your life where you have expected everything to be 'good' from your perspective, and felt disappointed or angry when it wasn't? How can you realign your expectations with this truth? What is one specific trial you are currently facing that you need to reinterpret through this lens?

Meaning of 'Ahsana Kulla Shay'in Khalaqahu'
Al-Ash'ari answers an objection about the meaning of a Quranic verse on creation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the verse 'Ahsana kulla shay'in khalaqahu' refers to Allah's perfect skill and knowledge in creation, not an assertion of absolute physical perfection of all things.

Core Idea
Allah's 'ahsana' means He knows how to create perfectly.

Imam al-Ash'ari addresses a common question about a Quranic verse that some misunderstand as claiming everything in creation is physically flawless. He provides a clear linguistic analogy to show the verse actually speaks of Allah's perfect knowledge and craftsmanship. This lesson unpacks that answer.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and answer
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how the objector's question is framed and how the response immediately provides a linguistic parallel.
The objector is not named; this is a standard kalam style.
2
Understand the analogy with craftsmanship
The key move is the analogy: 'He is good at creating' is like saying 'So-and-so is good at craftsmanship,' meaning he knows how to craft. Reflect on why knowledge is central to the meaning of 'ahsana' here.
The Arabic verb 'ahsana' can imply both 'to make good' and 'to be skilled at.'
3
Apply the lesson to avoid misinterpretation
Consider how this interpretation prevents the mistaken belief that every created thing is physically perfect. Instead, the verse affirms Allah's perfect knowledge and creative power.
This connects to the broader theme of divine attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قال قائل : فما معنى قولِ اللَّهِ -تعالى-: ﴿أَحْسَنَ كُلَّ شَيْءٍ خَلَقَة [السجدة : ٧]؟ قيل له : معنى ذلك أنه يُحسِنُ أن يخلُقَ ، كما يقال : فلان يُحسِنُ الصِّيَاغَةَ ، أي يَعْلَمُ كَيْفَ يصوعُ . فأخبر الله -تعالى- أنه يعلم كيف يخلق الإنسان.
If a questioner says: What is the meaning of Allah's statement: 'He made good everything He created'? It is said to him: The meaning of that is that He is good at creating, just as it is said: So-and-so is good at craftsmanship, meaning he knows how to craft. So Allah informed that He knows how to create the human being.
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer. The objector asks about the meaning of Surah As-Sajdah verse 7: 'He made good everything He created.' The response clarifies that the verse does not imply that every created thing is physically or morally perfect; rather, it means that God is skilled in creating, just as one says a craftsman is 'good' at his craft, i.e., he knows how to do it. Thus, the verse affirms God's perfect knowledge of creation, specifically the creation of the human being.

C) God only creates good things.

Understanding 'Created Not in Vain'
Ash'ari answers an objection about the meaning of a Quranic verse on creation and purpose.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Al-Ash'ari's refutation of the misinterpretation of the verse about creation not being in vain, and his argument that God creates both good and evil with a purpose of reward and punishment.

Core Idea
The verse does not deny that God creates evil; it affirms that creation has a purpose of reward and punishment.

In this passage from Al-Luma, Al-Ash'ari addresses a common objection from those who claim that the Quranic verse 'We did not create the heaven and the earth and what is between them in vain' proves that God does not create any evil or vanity. He shows, through the verse's own context and additional arguments, that the true meaning is about the ultimate purpose of creation: reward for believers and punishment for disbelievers. He also provides two nuanced interpretations of the verse and counters selective use of Quranic evidence.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and initial answer
Start with the opponent's question about the meaning of the verse. Then read Ash'ari's response citing the continuation of the verse to show it rebuts the disbelievers' assumption of no afterlife.
Notice how Ash'ari uses the immediate Quranic context to clarify the meaning.
2
Understand the refutation of disbelievers' assumption
The key point: the verse refutes those who think there is no return for punishment or reward. Thus, creation is not vain because it leads to a final outcome.
The disbelievers are those who deny the afterlife.
3
Examine Ash'ari's two interpretations
Ash'ari offers two possibilities: (1) 'in vain' means God did not create the whole as vain because vanity is part of His creation, or (2) He did not create them as vain because vanity came after creation. Compare these.
These interpretations allow for the existence of evil while maintaining purposeful creation.
4
Analyze the argument from generality
Ash'ari uses Quran 25:59 to argue that God created everything between heavens and earth, including deeds. This counters opponents who selectively apply verses to deny that God creates evil.
The argument shows consistency: if God creates all things, He also creates vanity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قال: فما معنى قوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَا خَلَقْنَا السَّمَاءَ وَالْأَرْضَ وَمَا بَيْنَهُمَا بَاطِلًا﴾؟ قيل له: قال الله تعالى: ﴿ذَلِكَ ظَنُّ الَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا﴾ فدل ذلك على أن المعنى فيها: خلقتهما وما بينهما، وأنا لا أثيب من أطاعني، ولا أعاقب من عصاني وكفر بي؛ لأن الكافرين ظنوا أنهم لا يُعادُونَ، ولا لهم رجعة فيُعاقبون. فبيَّنَ الله تعالى أنه ما خلق الخلق إِلَّا وَمَصيرُ بعضهم إلى ثواب ورجوع بعضهم إلى العقاب. وأنَّ الكافرينَ ظَنُّوا ذلك؛ لأنَّه بَيَّنَ أَنَّ ذلكَ بابُ الثوابِ والعقاب؛ لأنه تعالى قال: أَمْ نَجْعَلُ الَّذِينَ ءَامَنُوا وَعَمِلُوا الصَّالِحَاتِ كَالْمُفْسِدِينَ فِي الْأَرْضِ أَمْ نَجْعَلُ الْمُتَّقِينَ كَالْفُجَّارِ، فأخبر تعالى أن ظن المشركين الذين أنكر عليهم: أنَّهم ظنوا: أنَّه لا عاقبةً يقعُ فيها تَفْرِقَةٌ بين المؤمنينَ والكافرينَ، بَاطِلٌ.

قال الشيخ أبو الحسن: وقد يَحتمل وَوَمَا خَلَقْنَا السَّمَاءَ وَالْأَرْضَ وَمَا بَيْنَهُمَا بَاطِلًا، أي لمْ أخْلُقْ ذلك أجمع باطلا؛ لأنَّ الباطل بعضُ خلقِ الله تعالى. ويَحتَمِلُ: ما خلقتُ ذلك باطلا، أي لم أجعله باطلا؛ إذ خَلَقْتُهُما؛ لأنَّ الباطل حَدَثَ بعد أنْ خَلَقْتُهما.

وقد قال الله تعالى: خَلَقَ السَّمَاوَاتِ وَالْأَرْضَ وَمَا بَيْنَهُمَا فِي سِتَّةِ أَيَّامٍ فَعُمُومُ هَذَا القولِ يدلُّ على أنه خَلَقَ ما بينَهُما، ممَّا حدَثَ من الخَلْقِ كالملائكة الذين كانوا بينهما، وما خَلَقَه بينهما مِنْ أعمالِ الحيوان في ذلك الوقتِ. فَلِمَ قَضَوْا بِإِحْدَى الآيتين على أن الله تعالى لم يخلق الباطل دون أن يقضوا بالآية الأخرى على أن الله خلق ما كان بينهما من فعل الملائكة وغيرهم في ذلك الوقت؟ ويقال لهم: إن كان قولُ الله تعالى في المشركين: يَلْوُونَ أَلْسِنَتَهُم بِالْكِتَابِ لِتَحْسَبُوهُ مِنَ الْكِتَابِ وَمَا هُوَ مِنَ الْكِتَابِ وَيَقُولُونَ هُوَ مِنْ عِندِ اللَّهِ وَمَا هُوَ مِنْ عِندِ اللَّهِ معناه:
If it is said: What is the meaning of His statement, the Exalted: 'And We did not create the heaven and the earth and what is between them in vain'? It is replied to him: God, the Exalted, said: 'That is the assumption of those who disbelieve.' So that indicates that the meaning therein is: I created them both and what is between them, and I do not reward whoever obeys Me nor punish whoever disobeys Me and disbelieves in Me; because the disbelievers assumed that they would not be returned, and there is no return for them so that they might be punished. Then God, the Exalted, explained that He created the creation only with a destination of some of them to reward and a return of some of them to punishment. And that the disbelievers assumed that; because He explained that that is the gate of reward and punishment; because He, the Exalted, said: 'Or shall We treat those who believe and do righteous deeds like those who spread corruption in the earth, or shall We treat the righteous like the wicked?' So He, the Exalted, informed that the assumption of the polytheists whom He censured: that they assumed that there is no final outcome in which a distinction occurs between the believers and the disbelievers, is false.

Sheikh Abu al-Hasan said: And it is possible that 'And We did not create the heaven and the earth and what is between them in vain' means I did not create all that as vain; because vanity is part of God's creation, the Exalted. And it is possible: I did not create that vainly, i.e., I did not make it vain when I created them; because vanity occurred after I created them.

And God, the Exalted, said: 'He created the heavens and the earth and what is between them in six days.' So the generality of this statement indicates that He created what is between them, from what occurred of creation, like the angels who were between them, and what He created between them from the deeds of animals at that time. So why did they rule by one of the two verses that God, the Exalted, did not create vanity, without ruling by the other verse that God created what was between them from the deed of the angels and others at that time? And it is said to them: If God's statement, the Exalted, about the polytheists: 'They twist their tongues with the Book so that you think it is from the Book, but it is not from the Book, and they say: It is from God, but it is not from God' means:
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage is a combined objection-and-answer followed by the author's own interpretive commentary and a further argument. The passage begins with an objection from an opponent (likely a Mu'tazilite) who asks about the meaning of the Quranic verse 'And We did not create the heaven and the earth and what is between them in vain' (Sād 38:27). The opponent implies that the verse denies that God creates anything vain or evil. The answer is given by citing the continuation of the same verse: 'That is the assumption of those who disbelieve.' The answer explains that the verse actually refutes the disbelievers' assumption that there is no afterlife with reward and punishment. The meaning is that God created everything with purpose: to reward believers and punish disbelievers. The disbelievers wrongly thought there would be no resurrection. Then al-Ash'ari (Sheikh Abu al-Hasan) adds two possible interpretations of the verse. First, the phrase 'in vain' could mean that God did not create the whole as vain, because vanity is itself part of God's creation (i.e., He creates both good and evil). Second, it could mean that He did not create them as vain, because vanity (evil) arose after creation, not as the original purpose. Then al-Ash'ari presents a further argument using another verse: 'He created the heavens and the earth and what is between them in six days' (al-Furqān 25:59). This verse's generality indicates that God created everything between them, including the deeds of angels and animals. Thus, the opponents cannot selectively apply one verse to deny that God creates evil while ignoring the other verse that affirms He creates all things. Finally, al-Ash'ari begins a reference to Quran 3:78 about the polytheists distorting scripture, but the text cuts off. The argument is that just as the polytheists falsely attribute their words to God, so do the opponents in their selective interpretation.

Key Terms
الباطل
خلق
ثواب
عقاب
ظن

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the verse 'not created in vain' means God does not create any evil or vanity at all.
Correction: Ash'ari shows the verse actually proves a purpose for reward and punishment, and evil is still created by God.

Checkpoint
According to Ash'ari, what does the verse 'We did not create the heaven and the earth and what is between them in vain' actually prove?
A) That God does not create any evil.
B) That there is no afterlife.
C) That there is reward and punishment.
D) That creation is pointless.

Key Takeaway
Al-Ash'ari demonstrates that the verse 'not created in vain' affirms a purposeful creation culminating in reward and punishment, and that God creates both good and evil.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face trials or see evil in the world, do you truly believe that God has not created anything in vain, or do you sometimes fall into despair and doubt His purpose? What would change if you lived each moment with the certainty that every event has a purpose in the final reward and punishment?
?
The disbelievers assumed there would be no accountability. In your daily life, do you act as if there is no ultimate reckoning? When you sin in secret, do you truly feel the weight of divine justice, or do you forget that your deeds are being recorded?
?
Al-Ash'ari teaches that even vanity (bāṭil) is created by God but not as the original purpose. How does this challenge your tendency to complain about things not going your way? Will you now accept that even apparent evils are part of a wise plan, and commit to patience and gratitude?

Allah Creates All Inner Thoughts
Al-Ash'ari answers a question about two twins and the source of their conflicting inner thoughts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Ash'ari explains that Allah creates both true and false thoughts in the heart, and why a true thought is not considered the speech of Allah.

Core Idea
Allah creates both true and false thoughts; truthfulness belongs only to His speech.

Al-Ash'ari presents a thought-provoking scenario of two twins in a desert, each experiencing a conflicting belief in their heart. This discussion leads us to the delicate question of the origin of inner thoughts and their relation to divine attributes. Through this dialogue, we learn how to affirm divine creation while maintaining the distinction between Allah's eternal speech and created human thoughts.

Guided Path
1
Read the dialogue carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the question-and-answer structure. The opponent asks about two twins and the source of their conflicting thoughts.
2
Identify the distinction between haqq and sidq
Pay attention to al-Ash'ari's response when asked if the thought is 'sidq' (truthful). He clarifies that sidq is only Allah's speech, not inner thoughts. The thought is true (haqq) but not Allah's speech.
This is the key theological point.
3
Consider the second twin's false thought
The opponent asks about the twin who believes in trinity. Al-Ash'ari affirms that Allah also creates that thought, implying that false thoughts are also created by Allah.
This shows that creation of false thoughts does not impute falsehood to Allah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۲۷- مسألة [في الخواطر] إن قال قائل: حدّثونا عن توأمين كانا في برّيةٍ، فوقع بقلب أحدهما أن الله واحد، من ألقى ذلك في قلبه؟ قلنا له: الله -تعالى-. فإن قال: أفَحَقٌّ ما ألقاه بقلبه؟ قيل له: نعم. فإن قال: أَفَصِدْقٌ ما ألقاه بقلبه؟ قيل: صِدْقُ الله -تعالى- لا يكون إلا كلامَه، وما وقع بقلب الإنسان ليس بكلام الله -تعالى-، فيقال: إن الله -تعالى- صَدَقَه فيه. فإن قال: فإن الآخرَ وقع في قلبه: أن الله ثالث ثلاثة، من ألقى ذلك بقلبه؟ قيل له: الله -تعالى-. فإن قال: أفباطل ما ألقاه بقلبه؟
27- Issue [Regarding Thoughts] If a questioner says: 'Tell us about two twins who were in a desert; it occurred in the heart of one of them that Allah is one. Who cast that into his heart?' We say to him: 'Allah—Exalted is He.' If he says: 'Is what He cast into his heart true (haqq)?' It is said to him: 'Yes.' If he says: 'Is what He cast into his heart truthful (sidq)?' It is said: 'The truthfulness (sidq) of Allah—Exalted is He—is only His speech, and what occurs in the heart of a human is not the speech of Allah—Exalted is He. So it is said: Allah—Exalted is He—made it true (sadaqahu) concerning it.' If he says: 'Then the other—it occurred in his heart that Allah is a third of three. Who cast that into his heart?' It is said to him: 'Allah—Exalted is He.' If he says: 'Is what He cast into his heart false (bāṭil)?'
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage is a question-and-answer dialogue (مسألة) about 'thoughts' (الخواطر) that arise in the heart. The opponent presents the case of two twins in a desert: one spontaneously believes 'Allah is one,' the other believes 'Allah is a third of three.' The opponent asks who casts these thoughts. The answer is that Allah casts both. When asked whether the first thought is 'true' (haqq), the answer is yes. When asked whether it is 'truthful' (sidq) from Allah, the answer clarifies a distinction: sidq (truthfulness) is a quality of Allah's speech, not of inner thoughts. However, it can be said that Allah 'made it true' (sadaqahu) for the person, meaning He caused it to correspond to reality. The opponent then asks about the second thought (the false belief in trinity): if it was cast by Allah, is it false? The text ends on that question, but the implied answer is that it is indeed false—Allah creates both true and false thoughts as a test or as part of His decree. The key point is that Allah creates all thoughts, whether true or false, but the attribute of 'sidq' is reserved for His speech; a thought's truthfulness is a created correspondence, not an attribute of Allah.

Key Terms
الخواطر
التوأمان
البرية
الحق
الصدق
الباطل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that a true inner thought is the same as Allah's speech, or that sidq (truthfulness) as an attribute can be applied to created thoughts.
Correction: Al-Ash'ari distinguishes: Allah's sidq is only His speech. A thought that is true (haqq) is not called sidq of Allah; rather, Allah makes it true (sadaqahu).

Checkpoint
According to al-Ash'ari's response, what is the status of the thought 'Allah is one' that occurs in a person's heart?
A) It is the speech of Allah.
B) It is false because it is not from Allah’s speech.
C) It is true in meaning but not called 'sidq' of Allah.
D) It is a creation of the person himself.

Key Takeaway
Allah creates all thoughts in the heart, but truthfulness as a divine attribute belongs exclusively to His speech, not to created thoughts.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever assumed that a strong conviction in your heart must be from Allah Himself, forgetting that even true thoughts are created by Him and that His truthfulness belongs only to His speech? How will you guard against equating your inner feelings with divine revelation?
?
When you realize that Allah creates both true and false thoughts in people, does that humble you when you see someone in falsehood? Do you recognize your own dependence on Allah to guide your heart, and will you ask Him more earnestly for steadfastness?
?
This lesson teaches that truthfulness is solely an attribute of Allah's words. Does your speech reflect that you revere His speech above all? How can you prioritize studying and speaking His words over relying on your own thoughts?

God Creates Belief and Disbelief, but Is Not a Liar
Al-Ash'ari refutes a misconception about God and lies using the twin example.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why God's creating false beliefs in hearts does not make Him a liar, and why His truthfulness is attributed only to His speech.

Core Idea
God creates belief and disbelief, but His truthfulness is only of His speech.

In this passage, al-Ash'ari uses a vivid example of two twins to clarify a subtle point about divine attributes. The question is: if God casts a false belief into a heart, does that make Him a liar? Al-Ash'ari answers that God's truthfulness is an attribute of His speech alone, not of His creative acts. This distinction preserves God's transcendence and avoids anthropomorphism.

Guided Path
1
Read the dialectical exchange
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Follow the back-and-forth between the questioner and al-Ash'ari. Notice how the argument develops step by step.
The passage is structured as a series of questions and answers.
2
Identify the crucial distinction
Note the moment where al-Ash'ari says that God's truthfulness (sidq) is only His speech, not what occurs in hearts. This is the key to the whole argument.
This distinction prevents attributing God's attributes to created things.
3
Understand the rejection of two extremes
When asked if God made the second twin truthful or lying, al-Ash'ari rejects both. Understand why: truthfulness is only for speech, and lying is impossible for God.
The argument uses the principle that creating a quality in another does not make the creator possess that quality.
4
Apply the analogy
Reflect on the analogy with power, will, and motion. Just as God creates power in others without being powerful by that power, He creates lies in hearts without being a liar.
This strengthens the point that God's attributes are not affected by what He creates.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۲۷- مسألة [في الخواطر] إن قال قائل: حدّثونا عن توأمين كانا في بَرِّيةٍ، فوقَعَ بقلب أحدهما أن الله واحد ، مَنْ ألقى ذلك في قلبِهِ؟ قُلْنا له : الله - تعالى - فإن قالَ : أَفَحَقِّ ما ألقاهُ بقَلْبِه؟ قيل له : نعم . فإن قالَ : أَفَصِدْقٌ ما ألقاه بقلبه؟ قیل : صِدْقُ الله -تعالى- لا يكونُ إِلَّا كَلَامَه، وما وقع بقلب الإنسان ليس بكلام الله -تعالى-، فيقال : إِنَّ الله -تعالى- صَدَقَه فيه . فإن قال : فإن الآخرَ وَقَعَ في قلبه : أنَّ اللَّهَ ثَالِثُ ثلاثة ، مَنْ أَلْقَى ذلِكَ بِقَلْبِه . قيل له : الله -تعالى-. فإن قال : أفباطل ما ألقاه بقلبه؟ قيل له : نَعَمْ . فإِنْ قالَ : أفصَدَقَه فيما أَلْقَاه بقلبِهِ أَمْ كَذَبَه؟ قيل : خطأ أن يقال له : صَدَقَه فيه ؛ لأنَّ صِدْقَ البارِي مِنْ صِفاتِ كَلَامُه [؟] وهو خطأ أن يقال : كَذَبَه فيه ؛ لأنَّ الكذب لا يجوز على الباري - تعالى - ؛ لأنه مُسْتحيل أَنْ يَكْذِبَ ، وليسَ يجب إذا خلق كَذِبًا لغيرِه ، و كَذِبًا في قلب غيره : أَنْ يكونَ كَاذِبًا ، كما لا يَجِبُ إِذا خَلَقَ قُدرةٌ في غيره وإرادةً في غيره، وحركة في غيره، أنْ يَكونَ بذلك قادرًا مريدا متحركًا.
27- Issue [concerning inner thoughts]. If a questioner says: Tell us about two twins who were in a desert; it occurred in the heart of one of them that God is one. Who cast that into his heart? We say to him: God, exalted. If he says: Is what He cast into his heart true? It is said to him: Yes. If he says: Is it truthful (sidq) what He cast into his heart? It is said: The truthfulness (sidq) of God, exalted, is only His speech, and what occurs in the heart of a human is not the speech of God, exalted. So it is said: God, exalted, made him truthful (saddaqahu) concerning it. If he says: As for the other, it occurred in his heart that God is the third of three. Who cast that into his heart? It is said to him: God, exalted. If he says: Is what He cast into his heart false? It is said to him: Yes. If he says: Did He make him truthful (saddaqahu) concerning what He cast into his heart or make him lying (kadhabahu)? It is said: It is wrong to say that He made him truthful concerning it, because the truthfulness of the Creator is among the attributes of His speech. And it is wrong to say that He made him lying concerning it, because lying is not permissible for the Creator, exalted; because it is impossible for Him to lie. And it is not necessary, if He creates a lie for another, and a lie in the heart of another, that He should be a liar, just as it is not necessary, if He creates power in another and will in another and motion in another, that He should thereby be powerful, willing, moving.
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage is a dialectical proof (objection-and-answer) concerning the origin of inner thoughts (khawatir) and their relation to divine attributes. Al-Ash'ari presents a hypothetical question about two twins in a desert: one spontaneously believes that God is one, the other that God is a third of three (Trinity). The questioner asks: Who cast these beliefs into their hearts? The answer is that God cast both. The questioner then presses: Is the first belief true? Yes. Is it truthful (sidq)? Here al-Ash'ari makes a crucial distinction: God's truthfulness (sidq) is an attribute of His speech, not of His actions. What occurs in the heart is not God's speech, so we say God 'made him truthful' (saddaqahu) regarding that content, but we do not call the content itself 'God's truthfulness'. For the second twin, the belief is false. The questioner then asks: Did God make him truthful or lying concerning that false belief? Al-Ash'ari responds by rejecting both alternatives. It is wrong to say God made him truthful, because truthfulness is only attributed to God's speech. And it is wrong to say God made him lying, because lying is impossible for God. God creates a lie in the heart of another, but that does not make Him a liar. Analogically, God creates power, will, and motion in others without thereby being powerful, willing, or moving Himself. Thus, God creates both true and false beliefs, but His own attributes remain distinct from what He creates. The passage guards against anthropomorphic or unjust attributions to God, maintaining His transcendence and the distinction between Creator and creation.

Key Terms
خواطر
صِدْق
كذب
خلق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If God creates a false belief in a heart, then God is lying or is a liar.
Correction: God's truthfulness is an attribute of His speech only. Creating a lie in another does not make Him a liar, just as creating power in another does not make Him powerful by that power.

Checkpoint
According to al-Ash'ari, why can we not say that God 'made the second twin lying' (kadhabahu) when He created disbelief in his heart?
A) Because the second twin's belief was actually true
B) Because lying is impossible for God, even if He creates a lie in another
C) Because God did not create that belief; the twin created it himself
D) Because lying is only attributed to humans, not to God

Key Takeaway
God creates both true and false beliefs in hearts, but His truthfulness is an attribute of His speech only, not of His creative acts; thus He is not a liar for creating lies.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you find yourself holding a belief about God that might be wrong, do you ever feel that God is somehow deceiving you? How does this lesson challenge you to take responsibility for verifying your beliefs through His speech (revelation) rather than blaming Him for what enters your heart?
?
This lesson teaches that God creates both true and false thoughts in your heart. Which inner thoughts have you been lazily accepting as true without testing them against God's revelation? What will you do today to actively distinguish between a thought that comes from God's truth and one that is merely a created impulse?
?
If God's truthfulness is only in His speech, not in your feelings or intuitions, how urgently should you be reading and memorizing His revealed words? Name one specific step you will take this week to let His speech, not your inner chatter, shape what you believe about Him.

Divine Attributes

God's Creating a Lie Does Not Make Him a Liar
Imam Ash'ari answers an objection about God creating falsehood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why creating an act in another does not attribute that act to the Creator, preserving God's transcendence and truthfulness.

Core Idea
Creating an act in another does not attribute that act to the Creator.

Imam Ash'ari defends the Islamic creed that all acts are created by Allah. But a tricky objection arises: if Allah creates a lie in someone's heart, does that make Him a liar? This would seem to compromise His truthfulness. Ash'ari responds by clarifying the distinction between creating an act and being the agent of that act. The answer is both subtle and crucial for understanding divine attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without overanalyzing. Then read the translation. Let the author's reasoning flow.
The passage is dense with theological reasoning.
2
Identify the objection
The opponent presents a dilemma: if God creates a lie in someone's heart, does He affirm it (making Him truthful?) or belie it (making Him a liar?). Notice how the objection forces a false choice.
3
Analyze the answer's first part
Ash'ari rejects both horns. First, truthfulness is an attribute of God's own speech, not of what He creates in others. So affirming a lie in another is not divine truthfulness.
This distinguishes between creating speech and speaking.
4
Analyze the answer's second part and analogy
Second, lying is impossible for God. Creating a lie in another does not make the Creator a liar. The analogy: creating power, will, or movement in another does not make God powerful, willing, or moving in that sense.
The analogy reinforces that attributes belong to the agent, not the creator.
5
Synthesize the principle
Summarize: God's creating a quality in a creature does not mean He possesses that quality. This safeguards divine transcendence.
This is a fundamental principle in Ash'ari theology.

أَفْعَالُ العِبادِ مِن خَلْقِ الله قيل له : نَعَمْ . فإِنْ قالَ : أفصَدَقَه فيما أَلْقَاه بقلبِهِ أَمْ كَذَبَه؟ قيل : خطأ أن يقال له : صَدَقَه فيه ؛ لأنَّ صِدْقَ البارِي مِنْ صِفاتِ كَلَامُه . نَفْسِه، وهو وخطأ أن يقال : كَذَبَه فيه ؛ لأنَّ الكذب لا يجوز على الباري - تعالى - ؛ لأنه مُسْتحيل أَنْ يَكْذِبَ ، وليسَ يجب إذا خلق كَذِبًا لغيرِه ، و كَذِبًا في قلب غيره : أَنْ يكونَ كَاذِبًا ، كما لا يَجِبُ إِذا خَلَقَ قُدرةٌ في غيره وإرادةً في غيره، وحركة في غيره، أنْ يَكونَ بذلك قادرًا مريدا متحركًا.
The acts of servants are from God's creation. It was said to him: Yes. Then if he says: Did He affirm him in what He cast into his heart, or did He belie him? It is said: It is wrong to say that He affirmed him in it, because the truthfulness of the Almighty is among the attributes of His speech? Self, and it is wrong to say that He belied him in it, because lying is not permissible for the Almighty - exalted is He - because it is impossible for Him to lie. And it is not necessary that if He created a lie for another, and a lie in the heart of another, that He be a liar, just as it is not necessary that if He created power in another and will in another and movement in another, that He be thereby powerful, willing, moving.
Source pages p. 209

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer argument regarding divine creation of human acts, specifically falsehood. The objection is: if God creates a lie in someone's heart, does that make God a liar (if He affirms it) or does He belie it? The answer is that neither is applicable. Truthfulness and lying are attributes of the speaker Himself, not merely of what He creates. Creating a lie in another does not make the Creator a liar, just as creating power, will, or movement in another does not make the Creator powerful, willing, or moving in that sense. The point is that the attribute belongs to the agent of the act, not to the creator of the act in another.

Key Terms
صدق
كذب
الباري
خلق
قدرة
إرادة
حركة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that if God creates a lie in someone's heart, He becomes a liar because He is the ultimate cause of that lie.
Correction: The passage clarifies that creating an act in another does not attribute that act to the Creator. Lying is an attribute of the one who performs the lie, not the one who creates the lie in another.

Checkpoint
Why is it not necessary that God becomes a liar if He creates a lie in someone's heart?
A) Because God cannot create lies.
B) Because lying is impossible for God, and creating a lie in another does not attribute the act to Him.
C) Because God's truthfulness is not affected by others' actions.
D) Because the lie is not really a lie if God creates it.

Key Takeaway
God's creating an act in another does not make Him characterized by that act; attributes belong to the doer, not the creator.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
This passage teaches that attributes belong to the doer, not the creator. When you sin, do you see yourself as the doer? How can this truth change your repentance and your view of Allah's justice?
