Further Refutations: Inherence and Linguistic Arguments
Imam Ash'ari provides three additional refutations: inherence absurdity, linguistic analysis, and extension to will and speech.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Ash'ari uses the inherence model and linguistic analysis to further refute the objection.

Core Idea
If prayer inheres like motion, then every body part would pray; but prayer means supplication, which cannot inhere.

After establishing the conditional argument, Imam Ash'ari provides additional refutations that expose the absurdity of the objector's position. He first shows that if prayer inheres like motion, then every part of the body would be a pray-er. Then he points out that the linguistic meaning of prayer is supplication, which cannot inhere. Finally, he extends the reasoning to will and speech.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to understand the flow.
2
Analyze the inherence argument
If the pray-er is a pray-er due to inherence of prayer, just as a mover is moved due to inherence of motion, then every part of the body would be a pray-er.
This exposes the absurdity of the inherence model.
3
Examine the linguistic argument
The linguistic meaning of prayer is supplication (du'a). If prayer inheres, then supplication would inhere, which is impossible.
This shows the objector's own principles are flawed.
4
Consider the extension to will and speech
If God can perform prayer for another and be described as a pray-er, why not perform will and speech for another and be described as willing and speaking?
This forces opponents into inconsistency.

باب الكلام في التعديل والتجوير
بفرقان، لجاز لقالب أن يقلب القصة، فيزعم أن الباري يوصف بالقدرة على أن يجهل، ولا يوصف بالقدرة على أن يكذب. فلما لم يجز ذلك بطل ما قالوه.
فإن قال قائل: إذا أمر الله تعالى أن نصلي فصلاتنا هي حركاتنا، التي نتحرك إذا صلينا، والمتحرك متحرك لحلول الحركة فيه، والشاتم والكاذب إنما كان شاتما كاذبا؛ لأنه فعل الشتم، والكذب، لا لأن ذلك حل فيه.
يقال له: إن كانت العلة التي لها ألزمنا أن نجوز أن يكذب إلزامهم بمقالة أهل الباري - تعالى عن ذلك علوا كبيرا -: أنه أمر به، فيجب في كل شيء أمر به أن يجوز وصفه به، فإذا أمر أن تحل في أنفسنا حركات نتحرك بها، وصلاة نصلي بها، لزم أن يجوز أن تحل في نفسه حركات يتحرك بها، وصلاة يصلي بها، اللهم إلا أن يقولوا: إذا جاز أن يأمر الباري غيره بالكذب، فلم لا يجوز أن يفعل كذبا يكون به غيره كاذبا؟ كما إذا أمر غيره أن يصلي، جاز أن يفعل لغيره صلاة كان غيره بها مصليا. فإن سألونا عن هذا السؤال على هذا الوجه فهذا ما لا ينكر.
على أنه إن كان المصلي مصليا لحلول الصلاة فيه، كما أن المتحرك متحرك لحلول الحركة فيه، فواجب أن يكون كل جزء من الإنسان مصليا، كما كان كل جزء منه - إذا حلته الحركة - متحركا.
ويقال لهم: الصلاة في اللغة هي: الدعاء، فإن كان المصلي مصليا لحلول الصلاة فيه، فيجب أن يكون داعيا لحلول الدعاء فيه، وهذا فاسد عندهم.
ثم يقال لهم: إذا جاز أن يفعل الباري تعالى صلاة لغيره ويكون بها مصليا، فلم لا يفعل لغيره إرادة يكون بها مريدا، وكلاما يكون به متكلما؟
Chapter on Speech about Declaring Just and Unjust.
With a distinguishing criterion, it would be possible for an adversary to invert the story and claim that the Creator is described as having power to be ignorant, but is not described as having power to lie. But when that is not permissible, what they said is invalid.
If someone says: When God – exalted – commands us to pray, our prayer is our movements which we perform when we pray, and the mover is moved due to motion inhering in it, while the insulter and liar are only insulters and liars because they performed insult and lying, not because that inheres in them.
It is said to him: If the reason for which we obligated ourselves to allow that He can lie is the implication of the statement of the people of the Creator – exalted be He above that greatly – that He commanded it, then it must be for every thing He commands that it is permissible to describe Him with it. So when He commands that movements by which we move and prayer by which we pray inhere in ourselves, it follows that it is permissible that movements by which He moves and prayer by which He prays inhere in Himself, unless they say: Since it is permissible for the Creator to command another to lie, why is it not permissible for Him to perform a lie by which another becomes a liar? Just as when He commanded another to pray, it is permissible for Him to perform for another a prayer by which that other becomes a pray-er. If they ask us this question in this manner, this is not objectionable.
Moreover, if the pray-er is a pray-er due to the inherence of prayer in him, just as the mover is moved due to the inherence of motion in him, then it necessarily follows that every part of the human being is a pray-er, just as every part of him – when motion inheres in it – is moved.
And it is said to them: Prayer in language is supplication. If the pray-er is a pray-er due to the inherence of prayer in him, then it must be that he is a supplicant due to the inherence of supplication in him, and this is corrupt according to them.
Then it is said to them: If it is permissible for the Creator – exalted – to perform prayer for another and thereby be a pray-er, why does He not perform for another desire by which He would be desiring, and speech by which He would be speaking?
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage is a dialectical argument within the chapter on declaring things just and unjust. The author first sets up a hypothetical: if there were a distinguishing criterion (furqān) between cases, an opponent could invert the argument and claim that God can be described as capable of ignorance but not of lying. Since this is not valid, the opponent's initial claim is defeated.

Then an objector speaks: When God commands prayer, our prayer consists of our own movements, and the agent undergoing movement is moved because motion inheres in it. But the insulter and liar are so called because they perform the act, not because the act inheres in their essence. The objector implies that God's command does not necessitate that He be described with the commanded attribute.

The author responds: If the reason we were forced to allow that God could lie is because He commands it (as the opponents claimed), then for every thing He commands, it must be permissible to describe Him with that thing. Thus, if He commands movements and prayer to inhere in us, then it must be permissible for movements and prayer to inhere in Him. The author then adds an exception (illa an yaqūlū): if the opponents say that God can command another to lie but not Himself do it, then why can't He perform a lie that makes another a liar? Just as He can command another to pray and that other becomes a pray-er, so too could God perform a lie that makes another a liar. The author says this objection is not objectionable (mā lā yunkar), meaning it is a valid question that the opponents must answer.

Next, the author provides further refutations: First, if being a pray-er is due to the inherence of prayer (like motion), then every part of the human would be a pray-er, which is absurd. Second, the linguistic meaning of prayer is supplication; if inherence were the cause, then every part would be supplicating, which is false. Finally, the author extends the reasoning: if God can create prayer in another and thereby be a pray-er, why can't He create will or speech in another and thereby be described as willing or speaking? This forces the opponents to either accept the consequences or abandon their position.

Key Terms
حلول
صلاة
دعاء
إرادة
كلام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that prayer is primarily a physical action that inheres in the body.
Correction: Ash'ari shows that inherence would lead to absurdities and that the linguistic meaning of prayer is supplication, not physical inherence.

Checkpoint
According to Ash'ari's second refutation, what is the linguistic meaning of prayer?
A) Movement
B) Supplication
C) Worship
D) Inherence

Key Takeaway
The inherence model leads to absurdities, and the linguistic meaning of prayer as supplication undermines the objector's position, while the extension to other attributes reveals inconsistency.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you pray, do you ever think that your prayer is just a movement or a habit that 'inheres' in you, or do you see it as a conscious act of worship directed to Allah? This passage shows that prayer is a relationship requiring intention, not a mere accident. How will you renew your intention in every prayer starting today?
?
The opponents thought that describing God as 'pray-er' by creating prayer in another was valid. Are there any beliefs you hold about Allah that you have not examined carefully, assuming they are fine just because they are common? Identify one such belief and commit to studying it from the Qur'an and Sunnah this week.
?
Ash'ari's third argument forces consistency: if God can be described by what He creates, then He would be desiring and speaking by created things. Yet Muslims unanimously reject that. Is there any inconsistency in your own understanding of Allah's attributes? Write down one area and resolve to seek clarity.

God's Command and the Prayer Analogy
Ash'ari presents and answers an objection about God commanding falsehood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ash'ari handles an objection about God commanding falsehood and the role of analogy in theological argument.

Core Idea
God's command does not imply He creates the act in the commanded.

This passage presents a theological objection that tries to extend God's command to create falsehood. The objector uses an analogy with prayer: if God can command prayer and create prayer in the person, why can't He command falsehood and create falsehood? Ash'ari's response is subtle: he does not reject the question outright but shows it is not a valid proof when posed in this manner. Let's examine the argument and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then the translation. Notice the structure: an objection followed by an answer.
The passage is a single sentence in Arabic; it contains a question and a response.
2
Identify the objection and analogy
Find the objector's claim: if God can command falsehood, He can create falsehood. Note the analogy with prayer: as God can create prayer in the commanded, so He can create falsehood.
3
Understand Ash'ari's answer
Ash'ari says that if the question is posed in this way, it is not objectionable. Reflect on why: the analogy does not force a conclusion because commanding and creating are different acts.
Ash'ari does not concede the point; he shows the reasoning is not a proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جازَ أن يأمُرَ البارِي غيرَه بِالكَذِبِ، فلِمَ لا يَجوز أن يَفْعَلَ كَذِبًا يكون به غيرُه كاذبًا؟ كما إذَا أَمَرَ غَيْرَه أَنْ يُصلِّي، جازَ أَن يَفْعَلَ لغيره صلاة كان غيره بها مصليّا. فَإِنْ سألُونا عن هذا السؤالِ على هذا الوَجْهِ فهذا ما لا يُنكَرُ .
It is permissible for the Creator to command another to lie, so why is it not permissible for Him to do a lie by which another becomes a liar? Just as when He commanded another to pray, it was permissible for Him to make for another a prayer by which the other became a prayer-performer. If they ask us this question in this way, then this is not objectionable.
Source pages p. 256

Commentary
This passage presents an objection and its answer. The objector argues by analogy: if it is permissible for God to command someone to lie, it should also be permissible for Him to create a lie in someone so that the person becomes a liar. He gives the example of prayer: when God commands someone to pray, He can create prayer in that person so that he becomes a prayer-performer. The answer is that if the question is posed in this manner, it is not objectionable — implying that the analogy does not hold or that the premise is accepted but the conclusion is not necessary.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The objection proves that commanding falsehood implies creating falsehood.
Correction: Ash'ari shows that the analogy does not force the conclusion; the question as posed is not a valid proof.

Checkpoint

B) The analogy of creating movement in a moving object.
C) The analogy of a lover's involuntary love.
D) The analogy of sleep-talkers.

Key Takeaway
Ash'ari shows that an objection based on analogy does not constitute a valid proof unless the analogy is exact.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The objector used logic to justify falsehood. Have you ever twisted reasoning to permit a sin you wanted to commit? Will you repent of that self-deception and commit to obeying God's command even when your intellect protests?

Refuting Inherence: From Prayer to Divine Attributes
Ash'ari refutes inherence and extends the prayer analogy to will and speech.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ash'ari refutes the doctrine of inherence (ḥulūl) in actions and extends the analogy to defend the eternal nature of divine attributes like will and speech.

Core Idea
Inherence in actions leads to absurdity; God's attributes are not like human actions.

Ash'ari tackles the problem of how actions and attributes qualify agents. If we say a person performs prayer because prayer 'inheres' in him, then every part of his body would be praying—an obvious absurdity. By analyzing the language of prayer and extending the logic, he establishes that God's attributes, like will and speech, are eternal and not subject to inherence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation once to get the flow of Ash'ari's argument.
Notice the logical structure: if-then statements leading to absurdity.
2
Understand the inherence problem
Identify the parallel between prayer and movement. Why does Ash'ari say every part must be a performer if inherence is true?
3
Analyze the linguistic twist
Ash'ari uses the definition of prayer as supplication. How does this strengthen his refutation? Why is supplication not something that can inhere?
4
Extend to divine attributes
The final sentence extends the argument: if God can create prayer in another, why not will and speech? What does this imply about the nature of God's attributes?
This challenges the opponent to be consistent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عَلَى أَنَّه إن كان [المصلِّي] مُصلِّيا لحلول الصلاة فيه، كما أنَّ المتحرّكَ مُتحرِّك لحلولِ الحَرَكَةِ فيه، فواجبٌ أَنْ يكونَ كلُّ جُزءٍ من الإنسانِ مُصليا، كَمَا كَانَ كُلُّ جزءٍ منه - إذا حلَّتْه الحركة - مُتحرّكًا. ويُقالُ لَهُم: الصَّلاةُ في اللغة هي: الدُّعاءُ، فَإِنْ كَانَ المُصلِّي مصلّيّا لحُلُولِ الصَّلاةِ فِيهِ، فَيَجِبُ أَنْ يكونَ داعيًا لحُلُولِ الدُّعاءِ فيه، وهذا فاسِد عندَهم. ثُمَّ يُقالُ لهم: إذا جازَ أن يفعل الباري -تعالى- صَلاةً لغيره ويكون بها مُصلِّيا، فلِمَ لا يفعلُ لغَيْرِه إرادة يكون بها مُريدا، وكلاما يكونُ به مُتكلّما ؟
Further, if the prayer-performer is a prayer-performer due to the inherence of prayer in him, just as the mover is moving due to the inherence of movement in him, then it is necessary that every part of the human be a prayer-performer, just as every part of him — when movement inheres in him — is moving. And it is said to them: Prayer in language is supplication. So if the prayer-performer is a prayer-performer due to the inherence of prayer in him, then it is necessary that he be a supplicant due to the inherence of supplication in him, and this is false according to them. Then it is said to them: If it is permissible for the Creator to make a prayer for another so that he becomes a prayer-performer by it, then why does He not make for another a will so that he becomes a willer by it, and speech so that he becomes a speaker by it?
Source pages p. 256

Commentary
This passage contains two arguments. First, Ash'ari argues against the view that one is a performer of an action due to inherence of the action in him. If prayer inheres in a person, then every part of him would be a prayer-performer, which is absurd. Second, he uses the linguistic definition of prayer as supplication to show the absurdity: if inherence made one a supplicant, then the inherence of supplication would be required, but supplication is not an accident that inheres. Then he extends the analogy: if God can create prayer in another, why can't He also create will and speech in others? This challenges the opponent's position on divine attributes.

Key Terms
المصلّي
الحلول
الحركة
الدعاء
الإرادة
الكلام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that actions qualify agents only through inherence (ḥulūl), meaning the action dwells in the agent's body as an accident.
Correction: Ash'ari shows that inherence leads to absurdities: it would require every body part to be a performer of the action, and it fails for actions like supplication which are not accidents.

Checkpoint
According to Ash'ari, what follows if we say a person is a prayer-performer because prayer inheres in him?
A) Every part of the person must be a prayer-performer.
B) The person must be a supplicant because prayer means supplication.
C) Both A and B.
D) The person must be a mover.

Key Takeaway
Ash'ari demonstrates that inherence leads to logical absurdities and cannot be used to explain divine attributes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you pray, do you ever feel that your prayer is just a mechanical act that 'happens' to you, rather than a gift Allah creates in you moment by moment? This lesson exposes the absurdity of treating actions as independent things that inhere. Will you, from now on, consciously ask Allah to create sincere supplication in your heart before each prayer?
?
Ash'ari forces consistency: if Allah can create prayer in you, why not will and speech? Do you ever subconsciously limit Allah's power by thinking He cannot change your desires or thoughts directly? Commit today to relying on Him for even your internal states, not just your outward actions.
?
The passage shows that inherence leads to absurdities like every body part praying. In your own understanding of tawhid, have you ever unintentionally pictured Allah's attributes as 'things' that dwell in Him, much like accidents in a body? Repent from any such subtle anthropomorphism and affirm that His attributes are eternal, not inhered.

Ash'ari's Dialectical Argument on Humility
Ash'ari continues the argument using humility to show inconsistency in the opponent's view.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ash'ari uses a reductio ad absurdum to challenge the opponent's view on the relationship between God's commands and His attributes.

Core Idea
Actions are defined by performance, not by indwelling of qualities.

Ash'ari continues his dialectical engagement, pressing the opponents on their earlier claims about prayer and indwelling. He now turns to the attribute of humility, showing that their logic leads to contradictions about God's nature. This passage demonstrates the careful reasoning used to defend the distinction between Creator and creation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the back-and-forth structure: Ash'ari presents a conditional, then anticipates two possible responses.
The argument is highly structured; each 'if...then' is a move.
2
Identify the initial conditional
Locate the conditional: if prayer is by indwelling, then humility should also be by indwelling. Understand the analogy being drawn.
This is the core of the reductio.
3
Follow the first branch (acceptance)
If the opponents accept that the heart is humble due to indwelling, then consistency forces them to say the tongue is a speaker and the heart is a willer in reality.
This shows the problem of attributing actions to parts.
4
Follow the second branch (denial)
If they deny indwelling, then by their own logic, God must be humble if He commands humility. Then see how they try to escape by saying God creates humility in others, and how Ash'ari counters with the analogy of lying.
This forces a consistent definition: an agent is defined by acting.
5
Conclude the argument's force
Understand that the argument does not claim God is humble, but shows the opponent's position leads to absurdity. The final move establishes that 'humble' and 'liar' are defined by performing the act.
This is a classic kalam reductio.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم يقال لهم: إن كان المصلي مصليا لحلول الصلاة فيه، أفليس الخاضع خاضعا عندكم لحلول الخضوع فيه؛ لأن الخضوع يكون في القلب، والإنسان بكماله خاضع؟ فإن ادعوا أن القلب خاضع خاشع، ألزمناهم أن يكون اللسان متكلما في الحقيقة، والقلب مريدا في الحقيقة. وإن قالوا: الخاضع لم يكن خاضعا لحلول الخضوع فيه. قيل لهم: فإذا أمر الله تعالى أن نخضع فيجب على قياسكم أن يخضع هو. فإن قالوا: لا، ولكنه يفعل خضوعا لغيره. قيل لهم: وكذلك إن أمرنا بالكذب فجائز أن يفعل كذبا لغيره. فإن قالوا: الكاذب كاذب؛ لأنه فعل الكذب. قيل لهم مثل ذلك في الخاضع.
Then it is said to them: If the one who prays is a prayer-offerer due to the indwelling of prayer in him, is not the one who is humble humble according to you due to the indwelling of humility in him? Because humility is in the heart, and the whole person is humble. So if they claim that the heart is humble and submissive, we oblige them to say that the tongue is a speaker in reality and the heart is a willer in reality. And if they say: The humble is not humble due to the indwelling of humility in him. It is said to them: Then if God Almighty commands us to be humble, it would be necessary according to your analogy that He be humble. So if they say: No, but He creates humility for someone else. It is said to them: Likewise, if He commands us to lie, it would be permissible for Him to create a lie for someone else. So if they say: The liar is a liar because he performed the lie. It is said to them: The same applies to the humble.
Source pages p. 258

Commentary
This passage continues the dialectical argument. The opponents are pressed on their earlier claim that being a prayer-offerer is due to the indwelling of prayer. The response asks: if so, then being humble should also be due to the indwelling of humility in the heart. If they accept that the heart is humble, then consistency would require that the tongue is a speaker in reality and the heart is a willer in reality (i.e., all parts have acts). If they deny that humility indwells, then the argument turns: if God commands us to be humble, then by their logic (that the commander must possess the quality), God would have to be humble. If they try to escape by saying that God creates humility in someone else (not having it Himself), the response points out the same applies to lying: if God commands lying, He could create a lie in someone else, meaning He is not a liar Himself. But if they then claim that a liar is a liar because he performed the lie, the same would apply to the humble: the humble is humble because he performs humility. This forces a consistent definition: actions are defined by performance, not by indwelling. The argument aims to show the difficulty of maintaining a distinction between God's attributes and human attributes.

Key Terms
الخاضع
الخضوع
القلب
اللسان
الكاذب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The argument asserts that God is humble.
Correction: The argument is a reductio ad absurdum showing that the opponent's view forces the conclusion that God would have to be humble, which is absurd; it does not claim God is actually humble.

Checkpoint
What consequence does Ash'ari derive if the opponents say the humble is not humble due to indwelling of humility?
A) God must be humble if He commands humility
B) The tongue must be a speaker in reality
C) The heart must be a willer
D) The liar is not a liar

Key Takeaway
Ash'ari forces a consistent definition of action: an agent is defined by performing the act, not by possessing the attribute.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read that Ash'ari forces his opponents to be consistent, ask yourself: In what areas of your belief about God do you hold contradictions without realizing it? Are you willing to examine them honestly today?
?
If actions are defined by performance, not by possessing qualities, then your prayer is not genuine unless you actually perform it with your presence. How often do you pray with your heart absent? What will you do this week to change that?
?
The argument shows that wrong assumptions lead to absurd conclusions about God. What false assumption have you been comfortable with—perhaps about God’s mercy or justice—that you need to test against revelation? Will you seek correction even if it feels uncomfortable?

God's Command and Human Action: The Analogy of Prayer and Movement
Ash'ari argues that God can command lying without lying Himself, using analogies of prayer and movement.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ash'ari uses analogies of prayer and movement to argue that God can command lying without lying Himself.

Core Idea
God's command does not entail His own action.

In this passage, the Ash'ari master Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari tackles a key objection from the Mu'tazila: if God is just, how can He command lying? Al-Ash'ari responds by distinguishing between God's command and His own action, using analogies that are straightforward yet profound.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Notice the flow of the argument.
The passage is a refutation of the Mu'tazilite position on divine justice.
2
Identify the two analogies
Find the analogy of prayer and the analogy of movement. Note how each analogy illustrates the same point: God commands but does not act.
The first analogy: God commands prayer but does not pray. The second: God commands movement and creates movements.
3
Understand the logical structure
Recognise that the argument hinges on the distinction between God's command and His creative act. The command does not imply that God performs the commanded act Himself.
This refutes the Mu'tazilite claim that God's justice prevents Him from commanding evil.
4
Reflect on the broader implication
Consider how this argument preserves divine justice while affirming God's sovereignty over all actions, including human acts of disobedience.
This is a key Ash'ari principle in the debate on divine justice (al-ʿadl).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الكلام في التعديل والتجويرِ
لو أَمَرَنا أن نَكْذِبَ أَنْ لَا يَجوز أَنْ يَكْذِبَ هُوَ ، بل يجوز أَنْ يَفْعَلَ لنا كَذِبًا ، كَمَا جاز أن يَفْعَلَ لنا صَلَاةٌ ، ولَمْ يَجُز أن يُصلِّي هو فَقُولُوا في الكَذِبِ هذا القَوْلَ.
ثم يقال لهم : إذَا أَمَرَنا أن نتحرَّكَ جَعَلَ لَنا حَرَكَاتٍ نَتَحَرَّكُ بها ، فكَذَلِكَ لو أَمَرَنا بالكَذِب لم يَسْتَحِل أَن يَفْعَلَ لنَا كَذِبًا نَكْذِبُ بِهِ .
Chapter on the discussion of declaring just and unjust. If He commanded us that we lie, it is not permissible that He Himself lies, rather it is permissible that He creates for us a lie, just as it is permissible that He creates for us prayer, and it is not permissible that He prays. So say this same statement concerning lying. Then it is said to them: When He commanded us to move, He created for us movements by which we move. So likewise, if He commanded us to lie, it is not impossible that He creates for us a lie by which we lie.
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Mu'tazilite position on divine justice (al-ta'dīl wa al-tajwīr). The author argues that God's command to do something does not necessarily imply that He Himself performs that action. The first part uses the analogy of prayer: God commands us to pray, but He does not pray Himself. So if He were to command us to lie (a hypothetical scenario to test the Mu'tazilite position), He would not Himself lie, but rather create a lie in us. The second part extends the argument to the case of movement: when God commands us to move, He creates movements in us. Therefore, if He commands us to lie, it is not impossible for Him to create a lie in us by which we lie. The argument aims to show that the Mu'tazilite claim that God must be just and therefore cannot command evil does not hold, because the command and the act are distinct—God's command is a test or a decree, while the act is created by Him in the servant.

Key Terms
التعديل والتجوير
الكذب
الصلاة
الحركات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That God's command to do something implies that God Himself does that thing.
Correction: Ash'ari demonstrates through analogies that God's command does not entail His own action; He creates the act in the creature.

Checkpoint
What analogies does the author use to argue that God can command lying without lying Himself?
A) Only the analogy of prayer
B) Only the analogy of movement
C) Both prayer and movement
D) Neither

Key Takeaway
God's command to do something does not require Him to do that thing Himself; rather He creates the action in the creature.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God can command something without doing it Himself, what does that reveal about your own tendency to judge God's actions by human standards? Will you submit to His commands even when they seem difficult or incomprehensible?
?
Consider a time you obeyed a command begrudgingly. How does the truth that God creates both the command and the action in you change your view of your own obedience? Will you now see your actions as gifts from Him?
?
God's command to pray does not mean He prays—yet He invites you to pray. When you pray, do you truly feel that He has enabled you to do so? How does this realization affect your gratitude and reliance on Him?

Affirmation of Eternal Attributes and Their Nature
Ibn Khafif affirms Allah's eternal attributes and distinguishes attribute from described.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Allah's attributes are eternal, distinct from each other, and subsist in His essence without being identical to it or separate from it.

Core Idea
Allah's attributes are neither His essence nor other than it—they are eternal meanings subsisting in Him.

Ibn Khafif's concise statement establishes the Ash'ari position on divine attributes. He first affirms that Allah's attributes are eternal even before their objects exist, then distinguishes between knowledge and vision, and finally articulates the precise relationship between attribute and described. This passage is foundational for understanding how classical Sunni theology balances transcendence with the reality of divine attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and its translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the literal translation. Notice the three distinct sections: the pre-existence of attributes, the distinction between knowledge and vision, and the relation of attribute to described.
The Arabic uses parallelism to emphasize that attributes are prior to their objects.
2
Grasp the eternal pre-existence of attributes
Ibn Khafif affirms that Allah was Knower, Powerful, Seer, Provider, and Creator when nothing else existed. This shows that the attributes are eternal and not dependent on the existence of their objects.
This refutes any notion that Allah acquires attributes over time.
3
Distinguish knowledge from vision
The passage states that knowledge and vision are different attributes. Allah knows things before they exist, but only sees them when they exist. The non-existent is not seen and is not a 'thing' in the sense of being an object of vision.
This clarifies that knowledge is broader in scope than vision.
4
Understand the attribute-described relationship
The final sentence gives the precise Ash'ari formula: the attribute is not the described, nor is it other than the described, but a meaning (معنى) subsisting in the described. This is the middle path between identity and separation.
This avoids both anthropomorphism (making attributes identical to essence) and denial of attributes (making them separate).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويعتقد أنه سبحانه كان ولا شيء معه ، وأنه عالم ولا معلوم ، وقادر ولا مقدور، وراء ولا مرئي ورازق ولا مرزوق، وخالق ولا مخلوق . والعلم غير الرؤية، وأنه يرى الأشياء موجودة ويعلمها معدومة، والمعدوم ليس بمرئي ولا هو شيء. والصفة لا الموصوف ولا هي غيره بل هي معنى في الموصوف قائم بالموصوف .
And he believes that He, exalted be He, was while nothing was with Him, and that He is Knower while there is no known, and Powerful while there is no object of power, and Seer while there is no seen, and Provider while there is no provided, and Creator while there is no created. And knowledge is different from vision, and that He sees things while they exist and knows them while they are non-existent, and the non-existent is not seen nor is it a thing. And the attribute is not the described nor is it other than it, rather it is a meaning in the described, subsisting in the described.
Source pages p. 299

Commentary
This passage is a proof and explanation of the eternal attributes of Allah. Ibn Khafif first affirms that Allah existed eternally with nothing else. He then lists attributes that are eternal even when their objects are not yet created: Allah is Knower even when no known exists, Powerful even when no object of power exists, Seer even when no seen exists, Provider even when no provided exists, Creator even when no created exists. This shows the attributes are eternal and not dependent on creation. He then distinguishes between knowledge (علم) and vision (رؤية): they are different attributes. Allah sees things when they exist and knows them when they are non-existent. The non-existent (المعدوم) is not seen and is not a 'thing' in the sense of being an object of vision. Finally, Ibn Khafif clarifies the relationship between the attribute (الصفة) and the described (الموصوف): the attribute is neither identical to the described nor entirely other than it; rather, it is a meaning (معنى) subsisting in the described. This is the Ash'ari position that attributes are not the Essence nor other than the Essence—they are eternal realities that subsist in the Divine Essence without being separate essences.

Key Terms

علم
قدرة
رؤية
صفة
موصوف
معنى
قائم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that Allah's attributes are either identical to His essence or completely separate from it.
Correction: The passage clarifies the middle Ash'ari position: the attribute is a meaning subsisting in the described—neither identical nor fully other.

Checkpoint
What is the relationship between the attribute and the described according to this passage?
A) The attribute is identical to the described
B) The attribute is other than the described
C) The attribute is a meaning subsisting in the described
D) The attribute is created

Key Takeaway
Allah's attributes are eternal, distinct from each other, and subsist in His essence without being identical to it or separate from it.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Allah knew you before you existed and sees you now, why do you still act as if you are hidden from Him? What would change if you lived every moment aware that His knowledge and sight are upon you?
?
The attribute of being Provider exists even when there is no provided. How does this truth challenge your anxiety about provision? Are you more concerned with the provider or the provision?
?
If the attribute is neither identical to Allah nor separate from Him, does your worship reflect both His nearness and His otherness? Do you ever reduce Allah to His attributes or treat them as independent beings?

Eternal Attributes: Distinct Yet Not Separate
Al-Ash'ari affirms eternal attributes and distinguishes attribute from essence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Ash'ari affirms that Allah's attributes are eternal and real, existing before creation, and how he distinguishes them from the essence without making them separate entities.

Core Idea
Attributes are real meanings in the essence – not the essence itself, nor other than it.

Al-Ash'ari begins by establishing that Allah existed alone with nothing else – a foundation for divine self-sufficiency. He then clarifies that attributes like knowledge and power exist eternally even without their objects. Finally, he precisely defines the relationship between attribute and essence: neither identical nor separate, but a meaning subsisting in the essence. This passage lays the groundwork for the Ash'ari doctrine of eternal attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the repetition of 'nor' and the parallel structure.
2
Identify the three thematic parts
The passage has a natural three-part structure: (1) Allah's pre-eternity and attributes without objects, (2) distinction between knowledge and vision, (3) definition of the attribute-essence relationship. Find each part and see how they connect.
The third part is the doctrinal climax.
3
Focus on the key phrase on attributes
The sentence 'والصفة لا الموصوف ولا هي هي غيره بل هي معنى في الموصوف قائم بالموصوف' is the heart of the lesson. Discuss why al-Ash'ari rejects both identity and separation.
This is the Ash'ari via media – attributes are real but not separate entities.
4
Apply the concepts
Take the example of 'Knowing by knowledge'. How does this passage explain that Allah's knowledge is eternal even when no known objects exist? Reflect on the distinction between knowledge and vision.
This helps solidify the difference between eternal attributes and temporal objects.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويعتقد أنه سبحانه كان ولا شيء معه ، وأنه عالم ولا معلوم ، وقادر ولا مقدور، وراء ولا مرئي ورازق ولا مرزوق، وخالق ولا مخلوق . والعلم غير الرؤية، وأنه يرى الأشياء موجودة ويعلمها معدومة، والمعدوم ليس بمرئي ولا هو شيء. والصفة لا الموصوف ولا هي هي غيره بل هي معنى في الموصوف قائم بالموصوف . وهو عالم بعلم، وقادر بقدرة.
And he believes that He, exalted, was when there was nothing with Him; that He is Knowing while no known exists, Powerful while no object of power exists, Seeing while no visible exists, Provider while no provided exists, Creator while no created exists. And knowledge is not vision; and He sees things when existent and knows them when non-existent, and the non-existent is not visible nor is it a thing. And the attribute is not the described nor is it other than it, rather it is a meaning in the described subsisting by the described. And He is Knowing by knowledge, Powerful by power.
Source pages p. 300

Commentary
This passage explains the relationship between Allah's essence and His attributes. Al-Ash'ari first states that Allah existed eternally with nothing else—this affirms His pre-eternity and self-sufficiency. Then he lists key attributes: He is Knowing, Powerful, Seeing, Provider, Creator, even when their objects do not exist. This shows that these attributes are eternal and not dependent on creation. He then distinguishes knowledge from vision: Allah knows things before they exist (as non-existent) but does not see them because vision requires existence. The non-existent is not a 'thing' in the sense of an existing entity. Finally, he clarifies the nature of attributes: they are not identical to the essence ('not the described') nor completely separate from it ('not other than it'); rather, they are meanings (ma'ani) that subsist in the essence. This is the Ash'ari position: attributes are real and eternal, distinct from the essence yet not separate entities. The passage concludes by stating that Allah is Knowing by knowledge and Powerful by power, emphasizing that attributes are not reducible to the essence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think attributes are either identical to the essence (thus redundant) or separate gods (as Christians say of divine persons).
Correction: Al-Ash'ari says the attribute is not the described (not identical) nor other than it (not separate), but a meaning subsisting in the described – a middle path.

A) The attribute is identical to the described
B) The attribute is other than the described
C) The attribute is a meaning subsisting in the described, neither identical nor other
D) The attribute is a separate entity coexisting with the described

Key Takeaway
Allah's attributes are eternal, real, and subsist in His essence – they are neither identical to His essence nor separate from it.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Allah's attributes are eternal and real, does your heart truly acknowledge that His knowledge of your every thought existed before you were born? How would this change your private actions today?
?
The passage says the attribute is not the essence nor other than it. Do you sometimes treat Allah's attributes as if they are distant concepts, forgetting that they are real meanings subsisting in His essence? What one attribute will you meditate on this week to make it more real to you?
?
Al-Ash'ari emphasizes that Allah is Knowing even when no known exists. When you feel alone or unknown, do you truly believe that Allah's attribute of knowledge is eternally present, regardless of creation? How can you turn this belief into trust in His unseen care?

Affirming Reported Attributes without Anthropomorphism
Al-Ash'ari enumerates four points on affirming reported attributes without anthropomorphism.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Ash'ari affirms reported attributes like istiwa', nuzul, and hand without falling into anthropomorphism or denial.

Core Idea
Affirming divine attributes without tashbih is the Ash'ari middle path.

Al-Ash'ari now addresses the most sensitive area of theology: attributes that seem to imply a body. He shows a balanced approach—affirming the reality of these attributes while negating any human-like qualities. This passage lays out his method for istiwa', nuzul, and the hand, then generalizes to all such reports.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the four distinct points marked A-D.
2
Identify the four points
The passage presents four points about reported attributes. List them: istiwa', nuzul, hand, and the general principle for all such attributes.
3
Understand the principle for istiwa' and nuzul
Al-Ash'ari affirms istiwa' and nuzul as attributes, not as physical actions. Compare his wording: 'istiwa' not sitting' and 'nuzul not movement'.
This is the core of affirmation without tashbih.
4
Examine the hand attribute
The hand is affirmed as a real attribute, not a limb. Note the distinction: 'not with the hand of His power but with the hand of His attribute.'
This avoids both literalism and mere metaphor.
5
Reflect on the general rule
For all other reported attributes, the method is to accept the revelatory evidence in matters of the unseen without anthropomorphism.
This is the principle of tafwid or ta'wil? Here al-Ash'ari leans toward affirmation with negation of physicality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أ- إثبات الاستواء لا الجلوس والنزول لا الانتقال) ب ويعتقد أنه على عرشه استوى وأنه ينزل إلى سماء الدنيا عند الأسحار بمعنى الصفة لا بمعنى الانتقال . --جـ [إثبات اليد صفة لا جارحة] وأنه خلق آدم عليه السلام بيده لا بيد قدرته بل بيد صفته . د باقي الصفات الخبرية ] : قبول الأدلة السمعية في الأمور الغيبية، وهكذا جميع الأخبار .
A) Affirming al-istiwa' (establishment) not sitting, and al-nuzul (descent) not movement. B) And he believes that He has established Himself over His Throne and that He descends to the heaven of the world at the pre-dawn hours in the sense of an attribute, not in the sense of locomotion. C) [Affirming the Hand as an attribute, not a limb] And that He created Adam, peace be upon him, with His Hand, not with the hand of His power but with the hand of His attribute. D) The rest of the reported attributes: acceptance of the evidence of revelation in matters of the unseen, and likewise all [of the] reports.
Source pages p. 301

Commentary
This passage presents the Ash'ari approach to the so-called 'attributes of reports' (al-sifat al-khabariyya)—those attributes that, if taken literally, might imply anthropomorphism. Al-Ash'ari outlines four points under this heading. First (a): Affirming istiwa' (usually interpreted as 'establishing' or 'ascending') but negating that it means sitting (julus); similarly affirming nuzul (descent) but negating that it means bodily movement (intiqal). This is the principle of tafwid or ta'wil? Here al-Ash'ari seems to affirm the words as attributes without their apparent physical meanings. Second (b): He explicitly states that Allah's 'istiwa' over the Throne' and 'nuzul to the lower heaven' are to be understood as attributes (bi ma'na al-sifa), not as physical locomotion. Third (c): The 'Hand' of Allah is affirmed as a real attribute, not as a bodily limb (jaraha); when Allah created Adam with His Hand, it does not mean with the hand of His power (qudra) but with the hand of His attribute—implying that the Hand is a distinct attribute. Fourth (d): For all other reported attributes, the methodology is to accept the revelatory texts at face value while denying any anthropomorphic interpretation; such matters belong to the unseen and are to be taken as they come (hakaidha jami' al-akhbar). This is the classic Ash'ari stance: affirm the wording and the reality, but negate any literal anthropomorphism.

Key Terms
استواء
نزول
يد
صفة خبرية
تشبيه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some claim Ash'aris either deny these attributes (by metaphorical interpretation) or affirm them literally.
Correction: Al-Ash'ari shows a middle path: affirm the reality of the attributes as mentioned in revelation, but negate any anthropomorphic implications. The attributes are real but not like creation.

Checkpoint
How does al-Ash'ari interpret Allah's 'hand' in the creation of Adam?
A) As a literal limb
B) As a metaphor for power
C) As a real attribute that is not a limb
D) As a way of speaking that should not be analyzed

Key Takeaway
Al-Ash'ari affirms reported attributes as real attributes without anthropomorphism, accepting revelation's wording while negating physicality.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read that Allah created Adam with His Hand, does your mind automatically picture a human hand? How does this passage challenge that reflex? Can you genuinely affirm the attribute without forming an image? Ask yourself why it's hard to hold that tension, and commit to training your heart to submit to the revealed words without imposing your mental pictures.
?
Al-Ash'ari distinguishes between 'hand of power' and 'hand of attribute.' Have you ever reduced God's attributes to mere metaphors because they didn't fit your logic? In what area of your life do you tend to rationalize away God's direct action? Repent of that intellectual pride and accept the revealed ascriptions as real.
?
You believe Allah descends to the lowest heaven at the last third of the night. What does that mean for your prayer at dawn? Do you truly sense His closeness as a real descent—not a metaphor—or do you treat it as a figure of speech? If the former, how does that change your focus in sujood? If the latter, ask Allah to grant you the awareness of His attribute of nuzul so that your worship becomes a response to His nearness.

The Source of Divine Attributes: Revelation Only
Imam Ash'ari states the method of proving attributes is transmission, not reason.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that knowledge of God's attributes comes exclusively from revelation, not from reason or analogy.

Core Idea
God's attributes are known through His own words, His Prophet, or consensus — never by reasoning.

This passage from al-Luma' establishes the epistemological foundation for discussing divine attributes. Before any argument, we must know where we get our information. Imam al-Ash'ari clarifies that only revealed sources — the Quran, Sunnah, and scholarly consensus — can inform us about God's attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Notice the phrase 'طريق إثبات الصفات النقل لا العقل' which sets the theme.
2
Identify the three sources of attributes
The passage lists three sources: God's self-description, the Prophet's description, and the consensus of Muslims. Write them down.
3
Understand what is prohibited
The passage forbids taking God's names by epithet (تلقيب) or by analogy (قياس). Reflect on why these are insufficient.
4
Reflect on the role of reason
Ask yourself: why can't reason alone determine God's attributes? The passage implies a key principle of Sunni theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مُلحق (۳)
وهو عالم بعلم، وقادر بقدرة .
-
- [ طريق إثبات الصفات النقل لا العقل].
والصفات مأخوذة من السمع إما ما وصف الله به نفسه، أو وصفه رسوله، أو أجمع المسلمون على صفته، لا تؤخذ أسماؤه تلقيبا ولا قياسا. القرآن كلام الله غير مخلوق، والاسم والصفة ليسا مخلوقين. وكلام الله تعالى منه وإليه، مسموع ومكتوب ومحفوظ ومتلو ومدروس.
Appendix (3). He is knowing by knowledge, powerful by power. - - [The way of proving attributes is transmission, not reason]. And the attributes are taken from revelation: either what God described Himself, or what His messenger described, or what the Muslims agreed upon regarding His description; His names are not taken by epithet nor by analogy. The Quran is the speech of God, uncreated, and the name and attribute are not created. And the speech of God, exalted, is from Him and to Him, heard, written, preserved, recited, and studied.
Source pages p. 301

Commentary
This passage defines the source of knowledge about divine attributes and affirms the uncreated Quran. The author begins by stating that God is knowing by knowledge and powerful by power, establishing that attributes are real and not just names. Then he clarifies the method: attributes are taken only from revelation (السمع)—either from God's self-description, the Prophet's description, or the consensus of Muslims. They are not derived by giving God epithets (تلقيب) or by analogical reasoning (قياس). Then he applies this to the Quran: the Quran is God's speech, uncreated, and its name and attribute (being God's speech) are also uncreated. The Quran is from God and to Him, and it is heard, written, preserved, recited, and studied.

Key Terms
صفات
سمع
تلقيب
قياس

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that human reason alone can determine God's attributes and names.
Correction: The passage states that attributes are taken only from revelation, not from reason or analogy.

Checkpoint
According to the author, which of the following is a permitted source for knowing God's attributes?
A) Human reason and logic
B) Consensus of Muslims on a description
C) Philosophical speculation
D) Analogy from creation

Key Takeaway
God's attributes are known exclusively through revelation, not human reasoning or invention.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?

The Quran Is Uncreated: The Speech of God
Imam Ash'ari declares the Quran uncreated and describes its nature.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the Quran is the uncreated speech of God and that its name and description are also uncreated.

Core Idea
The Quran is God's speech, not created, and everything about it is from Him and to Him.

Having established that attributes are taken from revelation, Imam al-Ash'ari applies this to the most important attribute: God's speech. He affirms that the Quran is the uncreated speech of God and clarifies that even the terms used to refer to it are not created.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage focusing on the key words 'غير مخلوق' and 'ليسا مخلوقين'.
2
Identify the affirmation about the Quran
The passage states that the Quran is God's speech and is uncreated. Also the 'name' (Quran) and 'attribute' (being speech) are uncreated.
3
Understand the description of God's speech
The passage describes God's speech as 'from Him and to Him' and lists five ways it is encountered: heard, written, preserved, recited, studied.
These are physical manifestations, but the speech itself is eternal.
4
Reflect on why this matters
This doctrine distinguishes Sunni Islam from those who say the Quran is created. Reflect on the implications for the Quran's authority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مُلحق (۳)
وهو عالم بعلم، وقادر بقدرة .
-
- [ طريق إثبات الصفات النقل لا العقل].
والصفات مأخوذة من السمع إما ما وصف الله به نفسه، أو وصفه رسوله، أو أجمع المسلمون على صفته، لا تؤخذ أسماؤه تلقيبا ولا قياسا. القرآن كلام الله غير مخلوق، والاسم والصفة ليسا مخلوقين. وكلام الله تعالى منه وإليه، مسموع ومكتوب ومحفوظ ومتلو ومدروس.
Appendix (3). He is knowing by knowledge, powerful by power. - - [The way of proving attributes is transmission, not reason]. And the attributes are taken from revelation: either what God described Himself, or what His messenger described, or what the Muslims agreed upon regarding His description; His names are not taken by epithet nor by analogy. The Quran is the speech of God, uncreated, and the name and attribute are not created. And the speech of God, exalted, is from Him and to Him, heard, written, preserved, recited, and studied.
Source pages p. 301

Commentary
This passage defines the source of knowledge about divine attributes and affirms the uncreated Quran. The author begins by stating that God is knowing by knowledge and powerful by power, establishing that attributes are real and not just names. Then he clarifies the method: attributes are taken only from revelation (السمع)—either from God's self-description, the Prophet's description, or the consensus of Muslims. They are not derived by giving God epithets (تلقيب) or by analogical reasoning (قياس). Then he applies this to the Quran: the Quran is God's speech, uncreated, and its name and attribute (being God's speech) are also uncreated. The Quran is from God and to Him, and it is heard, written, preserved, recited, and studied.

Key Terms
قرآن
كلام الله
غير مخلوق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that because the Quran is recited and written in books, it must be created.
Correction: The passage affirms that the Quran is uncreated, and its being heard, written, etc., does not imply creation.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT true about the Quran?
A) It is the speech of God
B) It is uncreated
C) It is created because it is written
D) Its name and attribute are uncreated

Key Takeaway
The Quran is the eternal, uncreated speech of God, and its worldly manifestations do not imply creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You believe the Quran is the uncreated speech of God. But when you open the mushaf and recite, do you experience a sense of awe as if you are in the presence of the Eternal? If not, what is blocking that awareness, and what will you do to restore it?
?
Everything in your life—your home, your body, your career—is created and will perish. The Quran is not. How does this truth reshape your priorities? Are you investing more in the created or the uncreated?
?
You study the Quran, but do you study it as the very speech of the One who will question you in the grave? This week, before you read a verse, pause and say: 'This is from Allah and to Allah.' How does that change your readiness to obey?

The Khabari Attributes: Affirmation without Comparison
Imam al-Ash'ari affirms three khabari attributes and states the methodology for all such attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ash'ari position on the khabari attributes: affirming them as real attributes of Allah without modality, without ta'til (denial), and without tashbih (comparison).

Core Idea
Affirm the scriptural attributes of Allah as real, but without asking 'how'.

Imam al-Ash'ari presents the orthodox Sunni approach to the attributes mentioned in the Qur'an and hadith that might suggest anthropomorphism. In this passage, he addresses three specific attributes—establishment (istiwa), descent (nuzul), and hand (yad)—and then lays down the general rule for all such attributes. The key is to affirm them as true attributes of Allah without falling into either denial (ta'til) or anthropomorphism (tashbih).

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the original Arabic once, then read the translation. Notice how Imam al-Ash'ari combines affirmation with negation.
Pay attention to the structure: each attribute is affirmed, then immediately clarified with what it does not mean.
2
Identify the three attributes discussed
The passage mentions istiwa, nuzul, and the hand. For each, note how the author affirms the attribute while clarifying what it does NOT mean.
For istiwa: 'without sitting'. For nuzul: 'without movement'. For hand: 'not a limb'.
3
Understand the method: 'without comparison and debate'
The final part gives the general principle: accept all authentic scriptural reports about attributes with faith and submission, avoiding comparison and debate.
This is the overarching methodology for all khabari attributes.
4
Reflect on why this matters
This approach preserves divine transcendence while honoring the literal text, avoiding both extremes of ta'til and tashbih.
It is a balanced path that many later scholars followed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[الصفاتُ الخبرية ]
أ- إثبات الاستواء لا الجلوس والنزول لا الانتقال)
ب ويعتقد أنه على عرشه استوى وأنه ينزل إلى سماء الدنيا عند الأسحار بمعنى الصفة لا بمعنى الانتقال (۲) .
جـ [إثبات اليد صفة لا جارحة]
وأنه خلق آدم عليه السلام بيده لا بيد قدرته بل بيد صفته .
د باقي الصفات الخبرية ] :
قبول الأدلة السمعية في الأمور الغيبية، وهكذا جميع الأخبار الصحيحة التي رويت في الصفات يعتقدها إيمانا، وتسليما لا مقايسة ومناقشة .
[The khabari attributes] a) Affirmation of istiwa (establishment) without sitting, and nuzul (descent) without movement. b) And he believes that He is established on His throne and that He descends to the lowest heaven at dawn in the sense of the attribute, not in the sense of movement. c) [Affirmation of the hand as an attribute, not a limb] And that He created Adam, peace be upon him, with His Hand—not with the hand of His power but with the hand of His attribute. d) The rest of the khabari attributes: Acceptance of scriptural evidences concerning unseen matters, and likewise all authentic traditions that have been related about attributes are believed in faith and submission, without comparison and debate.
Source pages p. 301

Commentary
This passage is a classification of the 'khabari' (informational) attributes—those attributes that are mentioned in scripture but whose modality is unknown. The author begins by asserting that affirmation of istiwa (establishment) does not imply sitting, and affirmation of nuzul (descent) does not imply movement. He explicitly says that the descent to the lowest heaven at dawn is understood as a quality (صفة) and not as physical transition. Then he turns to the attribute of 'hand': it is a real attribute, not a limb. The creation of Adam with God's Hand is taken literally as an attribute, not metaphorically as 'power.' Lastly, for all other such attributes, the approach is to accept the scriptural reports (الأخبار) in matters of the unseen, believing them in faith and submission without drawing comparisons (مقايسة) or engaging in disputation (مناقشة).

Key Terms
الصفات الخبرية
الاستواء
النزول
اليد
مقايسة
مناقشة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Believing that affirming the attributes of hand, face, descent, etc. forces one to believe Allah has a physical body or moves.
Correction: Imam al-Ash'ari clarifies that these attributes are affirmed without modality: istiwa without sitting, nuzul without movement, hand without being a limb. They are real qualities of Allah, not comparable to creation.

Checkpoint
How does the author interpret the descent of Allah to the lowest heaven?
A) As a physical movement
B) As a quality, not as transition
C) As a metaphor
D) As a literal sitting

Key Takeaway
The khabari attributes are affirmed as real divine attributes without modality, and all authentic scriptural reports about them are accepted with faith and submission, avoiding comparison and debate.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read that Allah descends to the lowest heaven, do you feel a need to picture how? What does that urge reveal about your trust in Allah's own description of Himself?
?
Is there an attribute of Allah—like His hand or His establishment—that unsettles you because you cannot imagine it? Will you commit to affirming it simply because He told you, without demanding mental closure?
?
The passage says to accept these reports 'in faith and submission, without comparison and debate.' Where in your heart do you resist submitting to something Allah has said, preferring instead to analyze or debate it?

The Beatific Vision of Allah (الرؤية)
Al-Ash'ari affirms the vision of Allah for believers without spatial limitation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ash'ari position on the beatific vision: believers will see Allah on the Day of Judgment without any spatial or directional limitations.

Core Idea
Seeing Allah is real, but not confined to any direction.

This lesson presents a core belief of Ahl al-Sunna: that the believers will be granted the vision of Allah on the Day of Resurrection. Imam al-Ash'ari affirms this using the well-known prophetic analogy of seeing the full moon, while carefully safeguarding divine transcendence by negating any spatial or directional attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then the translation. Let the author's wording settle in your mind.
Notice the concise style and the list of directions negated.
2
Identify affirmation and negation
The passage has two clear parts: first affirming that believers will see Allah, then negating any physical limitations. Find each part.
3
Understand the analogy
The author compares the vision to seeing the full moon. Think about why this analogy is used: clarity, brightness, and collective visibility.
This analogy comes from a hadith.
4
Reflect on the negation
The negation of directions (front/back, above/below, right/left) shows that the vision is not like physical sight. Ask yourself why this is important for tawhid.
This prevents anthropomorphism.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[إثبات الرؤية ]
ويعتقد أنه -تعالى- يراه المؤمنون يوم القيامة، كما يرون القمر ليلةَ البدْرِ، لا يُضامُون في رؤيته، من غير إحاطة ولا تحديد إلى حد ، مُسْتَقبل أو مستدبر، أو فوقَ أو تحتَ ، أو يَمْنَةٌ أو يَسْرةً .
[Affirmation of vision] And he believes that He, exalted, will be seen by the believers on the Day of Resurrection, as they see the moon on the night of the full moon; they will not suffer harm in seeing Him, without encompassing or limitation to a direction, whether front or back, above or below, right or left.
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
This passage affirms the vision of Allah (الرؤية) for the believers in the Hereafter. The author uses the well-known comparison to seeing the full moon, a hadith. He specifies that they will not be harmed (لا يضامون) in the vision, meaning they will not miss it or be troubled. Then he negates any encompassing or limitation: the vision is not subject to spatial directions like front/back, above/below, right/left. This upholds divine transcendence while affirming real vision.

Key Terms
الرؤية
القيامة
المؤمنون
الإحاطة
التحديد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some people think that if we see Allah, He must be in a place or have a direction.
Correction: Al-Ash'ari affirms the vision but explicitly negates any spatial or directional limitation, showing that divine sight is not like physical sight of objects.

Checkpoint
What does the author negate regarding the vision of Allah?
A) That it is real
B) That it is limited by directions
C) That believers see Him
D) That it is a blessing

Key Takeaway
Believers will see Allah on the Day of Judgment, but without any spatial or directional limitations, preserving His transcendence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
1. Do you truly long to see Allah on that Day, or has your faith become merely intellectual? What would it mean for your daily life to genuinely yearn for that vision?
?
2. When you pray, do you unconsciously direct your heart towards a specific location (like the sky)? How does this lesson's negation of direction challenge your current practice, and what will you do to correct it?
?
3. If seeing Allah requires no direction, then His closeness is not physical. Are you willing to let go of all mental images of Allah to truly encounter Him in the hereafter? What step will you take today to purify your conception of Allah?

God's Absolute Will and Justice
The author asserts God's absolute will, sovereignty, and freedom from injustice.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ash'ari affirmation that God is absolutely sovereign, free from injustice, and that nothing can oppose His will or decree.

Core Idea
God's will is absolute; His justice is unquestionable.

This lesson introduces the core Ash'ari belief about God's absolute sovereignty. The author emphasizes that God is doer of whatever He wills, free from any injustice, and that His decree cannot be repelled or reviewed. This foundational principle sets the stage for understanding divine predestination.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage carefully
Read the full Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the literal translation to grasp the author's direct meaning.
Notice the emphatic style: 'فعال لما يريد' and 'لا يُنسب إلى الظلم'.
2
Identify the key affirmations
Locate how the author affirms God's absolute will, His rule without objection, and the irreversibility of His decree.
The text uses strong negations: 'لا اعتراض', 'لا مَرَدَّ', 'لا مُعَقِّب'.
3
Reflect on the negation of injustice
Consider why the author explicitly says God is not attributed to injustice. How does this relate to His absolute will?
This guards against the misconception that absolute will could imply arbitrary injustice.
4
Connect to the bigger picture
Understand that this affirmation is the basis for all discussions of divine decree (qadar) in Ash'ari theology.
This lesson sets the foundation for the next lesson on will and pleasure.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[ والقضاء والقدر]
ويعتقد أنه تعالى فعّال لما يريد ، لا يُنسب إلى الظلم . وأنه يحكم في ملكوته كيف يشاء بلا اعتراض، ولا مَرَدَّ لقضائه ولا مُعَقِّب لحكمه .
ويعتقد أنه -تعالى- يقرب من يشاء بغير سبب، ويبعد من يشاء بغير سبب. كل المحدثات بإرادته وخلقه. إرادته في عباده ما هم فيه، وبرضاه طاعتهم، والمعصية بمراده لا برضاه.
ويعتقد أنه يُعطِي وَيَمْنَعُ، وَيَذُمُّ وَيَمْدَحُ .
[Decree and destiny] And he believes that He, exalted, is doer of what He wills, not attributed to injustice. And that He rules in His dominion as He wills without objection, and there is no repeller of His decree nor reviewer of His judgment. And he believes that He, exalted, brings near whom He wills without cause, and distances whom He wills without cause. All originated things are by His will and creation. His will in His servants is concerning what they are in, and with His pleasure is their obedience, and disobedience is by His will not by His pleasure. And he believes that He gives and withholds, and blames and praises.
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
This passage outlines the Ash'ari position on divine decree (قضاء) and destiny (قدر). It affirms that God is active (فعال) according to His will, and He is not unjust. His rule in His kingdom is absolute without interference; no one can repel His decree or review His judgment. Then it addresses the concept of drawing near and distancing: God brings some near without cause and distances others without cause, emphasizing His absolute sovereignty. Then it states that all contingent things are by His will and creation. Then it clarifies the relationship between God's will and human actions: God's will is in His servants concerning what they are in (i.e., their states), and their obedience occurs with His pleasure, while disobedience occurs by His will but not by His pleasure. This distinguishes between will (إرادة) and pleasure (رضا). Finally, it affirms that God gives and withholds, blames and praises, indicating His complete control over reward and punishment.

Key Terms
فعال لما يريد
الظلم
القضاء
حكمه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that because God wills everything, He is unjust or approves of disobedience.
Correction: The passage clarifies that God is not attributed to injustice, and His will encompasses all actions, but He is only pleased with obedience, not disobedience.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is asserted about God's decree?
A) It can be repelled by prayer.
B) It has no repeller and no reviewer.
C) It only applies to believers.
D) It is subject to human objection.

Key Takeaway
God is absolutely sovereign, free from injustice, and His will is supreme and unchallengeable.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face situations beyond your control, do you truly believe that God's decree cannot be repelled? Examine a recent disappointment: did you internally object to God's judgment? How will you surrender to His absolute will from now on?
?
The passage says disobedience is by God's will but not by His pleasure. Does this distinction comfort you or challenge you? In what area of your life are you using God's will as an excuse for sin? Commit to seeking His pleasure over your own desires.
?
God brings near whom He wills without cause. Do you believe He brought you to this faith without any merit? How does that shape your humility and gratitude today?

Divine Decree and Human Actions: Will and Pleasure
The author distinguishes God's will from His pleasure regarding human obedience and disobedience.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will distinguish between God's will (irāda) and His pleasure (riḍā) in relation to human obedience and disobedience.

Core Idea
God wills all actions but is pleased only with obedience.

This lesson unpacks the nuanced Ash'ari distinction regarding divine will and human actions. The author clarifies that while all things occur by God's will, He is pleased only with obedience, not disobedience. This distinction is crucial for understanding divine predestination without attributing evil to God's approval.

Guided Path
1
Read the relevant portion of the passage
Focus on the sentences about bringing near/distance, will, and pleasure. Read both Arabic and translation.
The key phrase is 'والمعصية بمراده لا برضاه'.
2
Identify the two categories of action
Notice how obedience and disobedience are both under God's will, but differ regarding His pleasure.
Obedience is 'برضاه' (with His pleasure), disobedience is 'بمراده لا برضاه' (by His will not with His pleasure).
3
Understand the theological purpose
Realize that this distinction maintains God's absolute sovereignty while absolving Him of approving sin.
This answers the objection: if God wills everything, does He will sin? Answer: Yes, but He does not approve it.
4
Reflect on God's giving and withholding
Consider how the final sentence about giving/withholding and blame/praise ties into divine justice.
This shows that God's actions are not arbitrary but are part of His wise decree.

Source Text

?

God's Exclusive Creation of Effects
Al-Ash'ari denies natural causation and affirms God's exclusive creation of effects.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that according to al-Ash'ari, all effects are directly created by God, not by natural causes, and that human actions are acquired but created by God.

Core Idea
God alone creates every effect; natural objects have no causal power.

Al-Ash'ari begins by clarifying the nature of human actions and the world's events. He insists that nothing in creation acts by its own nature—fire does not burn, water does not quench. Rather, God directly creates each effect at the moment of its occurrence. This lesson unpacks that radical claim and its theological implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the causation passage
Read the Arabic passage from the beginning to 'الموت من الله تعالى'. Notice the repeated negation pattern.
Focus on the phrase 'لا تعمل بطبعها' - things do not act by nature.
2
Identify the examples
List the examples: water, bread, fire, eating, drinking, killing. For each, find what al-Ash'ari says about their causal role.
3
Understand acquisition
The passage starts with 'الاكتساب خلق الله'. Understand that human actions are described as 'acquisition' but are created by God.
This is the Ash'ari doctrine of kasb.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والاكتساب خلق الله لا خلق لهم، وأن الأشياء لا تعمل بطبعها، فلا الماء يروي، ولا الخبز يشبع، ولا النار تحرق، بل يحدث الله تعالى الشبع عند الأكل، والجوع في غير وقت الأكل، وهكذا الشرب من الشارب، والري من الله تعالى، والقتل من القاتل والموت من الله تعالى لا يدركه الوهم، ولا يحيط به العلم ولا ينعته العقل. هو الواحد الأحد الفرد الصمد له الأسماء الحسنى، والصفات العلى، له الحكم في الآخرة والأولى، وله الحمد والشكر والثناء والمجد.
And acquisition is God's creation, not their creation, and that things do not act by their nature, so water does not quench thirst, nor does bread satisfy hunger, nor does fire burn, but God the Exalted creates satiety when eating, and hunger at other times, and likewise drinking from the drinker, and quenching from God the Exalted, and killing from the killer, and death from God the Exalted. He is not perceived by imagination, nor encompassed by knowledge, nor described by intellect. He is the One, the Unique, the Individual, the Self-Sufficient. To Him belong the beautiful names and the highest attributes. To Him belongs judgment in the Hereafter and the First. And to Him belongs praise, gratitude, commendation, and glory.
Source pages p. 303

Commentary
This passage is a definition and proof regarding God's exclusive causation and His transcendence. Al-Ash'ari begins by affirming that acquisition (al-iktisāb) is God's creation, not the creature's. Then he denies natural causation: water does not quench, bread does not satisfy, fire does not burn. Rather, God creates the effect at the occasion. He gives examples: God creates satiety when eating, hunger at other times; drinking is from the drinker but quenching is from God; killing is from the killer but death is from God. This is a direct refutation of those who attribute causal power to natural objects. Then he describes God's incomprehensibility: He is not perceived by imagination, encompassed by knowledge, or described by intellect. He concludes with a doxology affirming God's oneness, attributes, and glory.

Key Terms
الاكتساب
خلق الله
طبع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think al-Ash'ari denies all causality, implying randomness.
Correction: He denies independent natural causality but affirms God's habitual creation of effects at the occasion of causes, preserving order as God's custom.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the relationship between eating and being satisfied?
A) Eating causes satisfaction by nature.
B) God creates satisfaction when eating occurs.
C) Eating and satisfaction are unrelated.
D) Satisfaction causes eating.

Key Takeaway
God alone creates every effect; human actions are acquired but not self-caused.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you last ate a satisfying meal, did you sincerely believe that God alone satisfied your hunger, or did you assume the food had power? Reflect on your reliance on means versus the Creator.
?
If you truly believe that fire does not burn by itself, how does that change your fear of hardship or danger? Are you willing to trust God's control over every circumstance, even when you feel threatened?
?
The passage says killing is from the killer but death from God. How does this impact your view of personal responsibility? Do you recognize that while you perform actions, the ultimate effects are God's alone—and does that humble your sense of control over outcomes in your life?
