Divine Attributes
beginner
4 min
God's Transcendence and Attributes
Al-Ash'ari describes God's transcendence and His perfect attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Ash'ari's affirmation of God's absolute transcendence and His beautiful names and attributes.

Core Idea
God is beyond all human perception and intellect, yet He has the most beautiful names and highest attributes.

After establishing that God alone creates all effects, al-Ash'ari turns to describe the Creator Himself. He states that God cannot be grasped by imagination, knowledge, or intellect—He is utterly transcendent. Yet He is the One, the Self-Sufficient, and possesses all perfect attributes. This lesson explores this balance between transcendence and affirmation of attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the transcendence passage
Read from 'لا يدركه الوهم' to the end. Notice the triple negation and the positive affirmations.
The three negations cover imagination, knowledge, and intellect.
2
Analyze the negations
What does it mean that God is not perceived by imagination, encompassed by knowledge, or described by intellect? Reflect on the limits of human faculties.
This is a classic Ash'ari statement of tanzih (transcendence).
3
Reflect on the positive attributes
After the negations, al-Ash'ari affirms God's oneness, self-sufficiency, names, and attributes. Consider how both negation and affirmation are necessary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والاكتساب خلق الله لا خلق لهم، وأن الأشياء لا تعمل بطبعها، فلا الماء يروي، ولا الخبز يشبع، ولا النار تحرق، بل يحدث الله تعالى الشبع عند الأكل، والجوع في غير وقت الأكل، وهكذا الشرب من الشارب، والري من الله تعالى، والقتل من القاتل والموت من الله تعالى لا يدركه الوهم، ولا يحيط به العلم ولا ينعته العقل. هو الواحد الأحد الفرد الصمد له الأسماء الحسنى، والصفات العلى، له الحكم في الآخرة والأولى، وله الحمد والشكر والثناء والمجد.
And acquisition is God's creation, not their creation, and that things do not act by their nature, so water does not quench thirst, nor does bread satisfy hunger, nor does fire burn, but God the Exalted creates satiety when eating, and hunger at other times, and likewise drinking from the drinker, and quenching from God the Exalted, and killing from the killer, and death from God the Exalted. He is not perceived by imagination, nor encompassed by knowledge, nor described by intellect. He is the One, the Unique, the Individual, the Self-Sufficient. To Him belong the beautiful names and the highest attributes. To Him belongs judgment in the Hereafter and the First. And to Him belongs praise, gratitude, commendation, and glory.
Source pages p. 303

Commentary
This passage is a definition and proof regarding God's exclusive causation and His transcendence. Al-Ash'ari begins by affirming that acquisition (al-iktisāb) is God's creation, not the creature's. Then he denies natural causation: water does not quench, bread does not satisfy, fire does not burn. Rather, God creates the effect at the occasion. He gives examples: God creates satiety when eating, hunger at other times; drinking is from the drinker but quenching is from God; killing is from the killer but death is from God. This is a direct refutation of those who attribute causal power to natural objects. Then he describes God's incomprehensibility: He is not perceived by imagination, encompassed by knowledge, or described by intellect. He concludes with a doxology affirming God's oneness, attributes, and glory.

Key Terms
الصمد
الأسماء الحسنى
الصفات العلى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that affirming attributes compromises God's oneness.
Correction: Al-Ash'ari affirms both transcendence and attributes, showing they are not contradictory.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which faculty can fully comprehend God?
A) Imagination (al-wahm)
B) Knowledge (al-'ilm)
C) Intellect (al-'aql)
D) None of the above

Key Takeaway
God is beyond all human grasp, yet He is known through His names and attributes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God is beyond your imagination and intellect, why do you still try to reduce Him to your own concepts? How can you worship a God you cannot fully grasp, and does your heart rest in that mystery?
?
You claim to praise God, but do you truly mean it when you say 'to Him belongs all judgment'? Are there areas of your life where you still judge others or yourself as if you were the final authority?
?
God has the most beautiful names—when was the last time you pondered one of them deeply and let it transform your view of Him and yourself? Will you commit to reflecting on one name each day this week?
